<Author>vws
<Content>Trust me, it's a great hotel... What is there to dislike about the Tapatio? It is one of the best hotels in the Phoenix/Scottsdale area and you can get a room for $95.00 until Jan. 5th (and around $220-50 after鈥ood breaks for AAA members). We have stayed at the Phoenician, The Hyatt at Gainey Ranch, The Wigwam, etc. Of all those hotels, we often prefer to go to The Tapatio because: 1. wonderfully friendly staff who go out of their way to say hello or to help you out. This includes the check-in staff, the hotel room-service delivery people, the gift shop people and the whole assortment of the people at the golf course (they could consider hiring at least one woman鈥ust to look as if they had an inkling that women can be pros, too). 2. The rooms are outstanding but not huge. There are two rooms in each suit. The first is, of course, the living room. That is separated from the bedroom by an ingenious systems of doors on either side of the bathroom (The bathroom has a pass-through from the living room to the bedroom鈥asin and mirror on one side, toilet and bath on the other with a door.) which is between the two rooms鈥ne that closes between the living room and the bathroom and one that closes between the bathroom and the bedroom; this allows people in one room to close off the other room but to still use the bathroom. The rooms are newly renovated鈥 read the earlier comment about what the writer thought were unattractive color schemes. Those colors are the hotel鈥檚 keeping up to date鈥any of the resorts we have stayed at in the greater Phoenix area, have begun to use similar colors. The beds have feather pillows and feather quilts. There is a wet bar and refrigerator in the living room. 2 wide screen t.v.鈥檚. AND鈥or readers鈥 first! Adequate lighting by each side of the bed. It is true that not all rooms are created equal. Some rooms don鈥檛 have great views (such as in the main building on the right side鈥?the view is of delivery trucks all day so avoid those rooms). It is a hotel which is built on hillsides (which is part of its charm). If walking is a problem (as noted in one of the earlier reviews) request a room down below. 3. There are several small restaurants and two larger ones. One of the two larger ones is all paneled with mahogany and is very handsome. Good food, reasonably priced for a resort. Great bar. Friendly atmosphere. Then there is their very slick 鈥淎 Point of View鈥?restaurant with terrific views of Phoenix/Scottsdale. The restaurant has gotten great reviews from food critics. Pricey but that is what a gourmet restaurant costs. 4. You want pools? They鈥檝e got pools. A huge water-wonderland set up with slides, etc. Two smaller pools nearer to the main part of the hotel鈥arely busy. One on top of the hill. Fitness center. And here is something outstanding: the hotel does not charge the usual $10-$12 a day 鈥渞esort fee鈥?which I have come to hate at all hotels. You can buy a special certificate for $2.50 a day for various uses of resort activities鈥ut you don鈥檛 have to. Right there you save at least $70.00 a week.5. GOLFERS! Listen up. The course is terrific. It is kept in first-class condition (with the exception of the 2nd hole鈥檚 green鈥ot sure why they haven鈥檛 attended to that). The course has been called 鈥渢he Phoenix areas best kept secret.鈥?The staff was very accommodating. The course climbs up and up until the 9th (at which point you are 3 miles from the clubhouse) where you can see for miles in either direction. There are some pretty tricky holes where doglegs, water and thick desert flora abound. Deep traps. Undulating greens, Fun. I wasn鈥檛 paid to be this upbeat about the hotel! I just think it is great place. It isn鈥檛 going to all things to all people鈥ut give it try. I think you will be pleased.

<Author>NoGuru
<Content>Like Niagra Falls We got a sweet $99 dollar a night deal for a three-night minimum. The weather was beautiful, the accomodations acceptable, the EIGHT swimming pools sufficiently resort-like, the food okay (except for the Pointe in Tyme Grille and Tavern, which was very good).However, this is not a restful property. It's right in the middle of Phoenix, along busy N. 7th St. Traffic noise is a factor and is masked by a series of fountains that thunder like Niagra Falls. Helpful booming generators are positioned throughout the grounds and collaborate with the fountains for a truly unique auditory experience. Several more irritants:1) Construction noise on the property's west side2) Our first night, our room was adjacent to an elevator shaft. Try to avoid this. The elevators are fussy and noisy.3) Housekeeping staff reporting to work at 6:30 a.m. and chattering at the top of their lungs.4) A room service employee flinging the contents of the previous night's ice bucket over a railing into one of the main courtyards. If I go back to Phoenix, I'll gladly pay more for a better property.

<Author>berchelm
<Content>Large, remodeled suites inside; Dated infrastructure outside I was in town for a business meeting, but due to Homecoming at ASU, my hotel in Tempe was sold out for the final night. I was looking for a mid-priced resort in the hills to relax and maybe do some hiking, so Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs seemed like a good choice.The rooms themselves are very nice. Mine was obviously remodeled, so the furniture was fresh, stylish, and the basic king-bed suite I had was comparable in size to a large Marriott Residence Inn or Hilton Embassy Suites room. Kudos to the room!The property itself, however, is very dated. The buildings look quite worn, and the property has a very claustrophobic feel because the buildings are situated so close to each other. The streets going around the property between the buildings are so narrow that only one car can pass by, and since cars must parallel park along the road in many locations, squeezing through is a harrowing experience.Like other reviewers, I found the food prices excessive compared to most hotels at this price-point, although the room service staff was very quick, friendly, and attentive.To be fair, I came to this hotel based on the pictures I saw on the Hilton web site, so it was my fault for not doing more research. Because I expected a new, state-of-the-art property, my expectations were not met once I got to the location and realized how old it is. I felt like it had a rather dark and dreary feel to it; it didn't have the new and clean look that I've become accustomed to in other parts of Phoenix. Because the room was so nice, it balanced out my overall impression of the property, but I definitely won't return for a second stay or recommend it to my friends.

<Author>smcalifornia1
<Content>Very Nice We just returned from Pointe Hilton and found it to be a wonderful place to stay. We have always stayed closer to the downtown area but have tired of all the noise and traffic. So glad we found this Hilton! It's true that it is located off the beaten path but that's exactly what attracted us to this resort. There is alot of up and down hill walking throughout the resort but if you find yourself in need of a ride back to your suite, there are benches for resting w/ phones available to call for a pick up. We liked the pool at The Falls and the bar area was a bonus although last call is at 4:45p this time of year. We ate at Pointe in Tyme twice and although it's a bit pricey the food was very good. The suites offer lots of space and 2 televisions are provided. The furniture (in our building) is bit outdated but the king bed was the most comfortable bed I've ever slept on! The entire staff are wonderful and friendly. We will now make Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs our regular place to stay during our annual trips to Arizona.

<Author>NashuaNH
<Content>Not impressed I attended a 5 day conference onsite sponsored by an employer. I travel quite a bit on business so I can compare offerings and expectations. There is no complimentary transportation from the airport, so prepare to pay either a towncar or Super shuttle both ways. Expensive and not expected for a large resort hosting business conventions on a regular basis. Internet is not free either and charged daily, whether you need basic or VPN. It was an extra $75 charge for me. Although the resort adverstises many restaurants, only two were open. There was nothing inexpensive and I paid $17 for a cheeseburger. The resort is not within walking distance of anything, so I paid a hotel employee through the conceirge service to take me to the closest supermarket and pharmacy. He was very nice and waited for me so I could get reasonably priced snacks and drinks for the week. The rooms were fabulous with terraces, nice two room suites and plenty of room. There was a mini bar in my suite with typical minibar prices.The elegant restaurant at the top of the hill was wonderful, attentive staff, nice food and a shuttle to your room. Beautiful view. That was a bonus. Another interesting point, I had a very early departure one morning so I went to the desk and settled my bill the night before. When I pulled up my bill a week later, there was an additonal minibar charge of over $50------ If I had not called, my employer would have paid for that or given me a lot of grief about some thing I didnt do. To their credit, there was no argument and I was told the charge would come off right away.So, it was a 50/50 kind of trip. All right but not great. Really too bad.

<Author>SeattleHotMomma
<Content>Perfect Trip for Travel with Toddler  Just returned from our family's belated summer vacation. Overall this trip exceeded our expectations. Here are some high points:- Room set up was great for our family of 3 (my son is almost 2). There were three distinct parts- family room, bathroom pass through, master bedroom with plenty of room to walk around the packplay/crib.- Our location on the property was ideal. First floor, facing the family pool, steps from The Falls. Our rooms were 1045/1046. They were back to back and not adjoining as we requested but in the end it didn't matter. I would HIGHLY suggest this building for families still using strollers or anyone that doesn't want to hike. The downside is you dont get a view from your room and no real balcony.- We got a crib, refrigerator and microwave (pay $15 for the stay for each of the last two items). We shopped at Safeway about 1/2 mile north of the property and ate breakfast and lunch in our room every day before putting my son down for a nap. Saved a ton of money. We dined out at night.- We brought our portable DVD player on the flight and the plug which allowed us to play my son's favorites on the nice flat screen in the living room when we were in the room. -Overall this seems like a great time to travel to the resort. The weekend was somewhat busy with a couple of weddings but no issue finding chairs around the pool. On the weekdays we were the only one in the pool until around 11am when a couple of others joined us.- The Falls pool was perfect for our little guy. The graduated entrance allowed him to play safely while we were able to wade a little deeper or sit down to keep cool. Better than a baby pool as we could all enjoy it together.-While my husband  son were sleeping I hiked every morning. It was wonderful and easy to access from the hotel area near the pool.-We did actually order room service twice and surprisingly it was affordable based on what we were eating. The kids menu is $5-$6 items and good. We got a pizza and it was good and $13-15. I got a open face steak sandwhich for $15 as well. Other items on the menu like drinks and dinner meals were outrageous. Kids breakfast at point in time was also a deal- my parents took my son so I cant comment on the adult food. My only complaints:-The directions from the website take you from the airport on 51 to Northern and then you drive through a really unattractive  rough part of town to get to the hotel. I would advise driving further to Cactus and going to the hotel that way. -The AC went out one day/night but the night manager was especially helpful in getting us a room for the evening in another part of the hotel with working AC and not having us move rooms entirely. In general for the $141 we paid a night I though the value was outstanding. My parents want to return next year at the same time.One other note: I am a huge fan of the Willow Stream Spa at the Fairmont Princess and would suggest if you are looking for a great spa experience I would go there for 1/2 day and get a treatment, workout, relax at their pool, spa lunch and leave the kids home. Its pricey but worth every penny.

<Author>Balmain
<Content>What a fantastic resort After receiving an email, while we were in New Mexico, from Hilton hotels telling me of a great deal for three nights including a Sunday at two Hilton resorts in Phoenix, as were were on our way to Phoenix (how did they know? - was it because I had made enqiries on the internet before leaving the UK?), we drove to the Pointe Squaw Peak, which could not accommodate us. If I have one less favourable comment, it is merely that I would prefer a smaller, easier-to-get-around resort, (the main pools were a long walk from our suite) but that said, it was great to be able to park very close to our room.

<Author>JRMAZ
<Content>Unless you WANT your weekend ruined don't stay here My husband and I live in the area and wanted to get away for the weekend, relax by the pool and enjoy what a resort has to offer. After much searching and review reading we chose the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort. We booked for a 3 day weekend. They were having a summer special $99.95 per night. We arrive on Friday about 5pm to check in. The front desk lady was nice and friendly but the lobby was over run by children jumping all over the furniture and a big crowd of teens. I gave the desk clerk my credit card. She said oops your card isn't being accepted. Well the cost of my 3 night stay was only supposed to be $333.00 and my credit card had plenty of credit on it. I gave her my debit card and we were registered and on our way. Later I checked my debit card online banking and discovered they put a hold on my debit card for $1200. I find this highly ridiculous. I understand and expect a hotel to put a hold on your card to cover incidentals, however my room was $99 a night for 3 nights, I don't see how a deposit 4 items the amount of the cost of the room was justified. We requested a king size bed. It was just me and the hubby. When we finally found a parking space, walked down a steep incline and found the building our room was in we opened the door to find they gave us a room with two full size beds in it. That was disapointing. Also within about 20 mins of turning the AC on there was a loud annoying clunking noise coming from the sink. We assumed it was some sort of water leak from the AC draning into sink pipe. It was so loud and annoying. We were already starting to get a little frustrated. We went back to the lobby and it was even more crowded than before with children, teenagers, and two weddings and their guests. We decided to walk around the property and take a look then go get something to eat and talk to the desk when we came back. Well.. this property is located on a mountain and the suites are built all up and down the mountain side. You can not walk anywhere without climbing up a mountain path. Unless you are 20 years old and in fantastic shape it's somewhat difficult to walk around the property. Especially in the dead of summer here it's 110-115 degrees. There is also little to no parking. Every parking space next to their nice waterpark, adult pool, family pool etc was filled up. The entire parking lot was filled to capacity so unless you want to wait to be crowded into an over stuffed van that drives you around the property to take you to the different areas of the resort you have to walk them which like i mentioned before is very difficult with all of the steep hilly inclines. So our nice walk around the property ended me being tired, huffing and puffing, and sweaty. I'm obviously not in tip top shape but that was just a little ridiculous. Our room was right next to a nice looking pool overlooking a the area below but we couldn't really get to it. The path to the pool from our room was up a very very steep road. So steep that it was just too much trouble to try to walk to the pool and since the parking is no existent it made no sense to drive to the pool. We went off property to eat and since the hotel is on a mountain we had to drive awhile to find any decent places to eat that were not in the run down part of phoenix. When we came back we had decided to checkout and find another place to stay the weekend. We went back to the hotel and called the front desk and told them we would like to check out early. They did offer to find us a new room but we didn't think we would enjoy ourselves. They told us they usually require 24 hour notice to cancel but they were nice enough to let us checkout the next day with no other charges ( i hope, as of now they have only billed us for the one night stay plus $12 for the use of the internet) So we are thirsty so my hubby said he's going to find a coke machine and get some ice. He comes back about 30mins later empty handed. We have a vending area right by our door but there is no coke machine. He hikes all around this hilly property to 2 different coke machines neither of which are working. He hikes from the hills to the gift shop in the lobby but it has now closed. There is nowhere else to buy a coke except order room service or drink from the mini bar. I'd rather not pay $3 for a can of coke but we were so thirsty we ended up drinking to cans of soda from the mini bar. I'm convinced the have non working coke machines to MAKE you buy the overpriced mini bar drinks. We could barely sleep all night with being thirsty all night ( you can't drink phoenix water unless you want to get sick) the loud clunking noise coming from the ac, the small full size bed for two people and the thought of our weekend ruined. We checked out first thing the next morning and went to the The Buttes Marriott resort in Tempe and that was the BEST decision we ever mad. I will give a review of that fantastic place next. The Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort is a hell hole that I wouldn't tell my worst enemy to stay at. I don't see how they have or keep any of their paying customers.

<Author>doggone31
<Content>OK but can be noisy on weekends Between the price I paid for the room and the Hilton name I was expecting an outstanding property. It was nice but not anything special.The good:- Large room, with separate sitting area- Good housekeeping- Proximity to hiking trails.The bad:- Room was a bit shabby (scuffed furniture), had no view, and overlooked the parking lot- Not much close by. You really need a car, although there's a Safeway and some shops about a mile north.- 5 pools, none of which are big enough to do laps in- Exercise room (for which a resort fee is charged) is underwhelming, with a limited selection of equipment- Party destination, not a luxury resort, on weekends. I stayed there Thu-Fri-Sat. Thursday night was fine. Friday night the people next door dumped a whole bag of beer bottles off their balcony. Saturday night, the same room was occupied by a different group who were up doing shots and talking and laughing on the balcony. I called the front desk at 1:15 and 2:15 and it took 45 minutes each time before things quietened down. On checkout, front desk staff were relatively unsympathetic (and the ass't front desk manager was borderline rude), saying, we have no control over who stays in our hotel rooms. True, but you do have control over how you respond to complaints, especially if your guests are paying over $125 night for your rooms.Overall, it's OK. I guess I was expecting this beautiful luxury resort and it's kind of just an ordinary hotel with a few more swimming pools.

<Author>physicx
<Content>Amazing grounds, room. Extras are extra. I stayed here a year ago for two nights. I would love to go back for the scenery and luxurious room.I met up with a friend who was here on business. Through travel rewards, she managed to get a King Presidential Suite which provided beautiful, condo-like quarters with design touches like high wood-beamed ceilings, a stained glass window in the bathroom and a nicely furnished and inviting balcony off the bedroom. The room was appointed with a fully-functional kitchen with full-sized fridge.When you walk into the room from an outside corridor, you enter into a great room with the high ceilings with wood-beamed ceiling. The decor was southwestern, and although southwestern decor is a little out of date and seemed so cliche for Phoenix, it felt fresh because it went nicely with the room's architecture. The layout: To the right in the great room is a large living room seating area with huge sectional and chairs with large coffee table. To the left of the door was a desk near the front window, and straight ahead towards the kitchen was a gorgeous dining table that would have been suitable for a formal dinner party. A little overkill (who would throw a dinner party at a hotel???) but I'm not complaining. Then, from the front door past the dining table was a kitchen. Although the kitchen was definitely a separate room, it melded into the great room as there was a bar counter/stools behind the dining table, so of course you could see into the kitchen from the great room.When you walk through the great room towards the bedroom, the kitchen is on the left, and then there is a nicely tiled, elegant half bath beyond the kitchen also on the left as you come up to the bedroom door. When you open the door, an expansive bedroom is revealed with large bathroom, double vanities and separate large changing area on the left. Bed on the right, and balcony straight ahead. Our suite faced west from the balcony and the colorful sunsets over the nearby hills were a real treat.I definitely could have lived here, no problem!The grounds were beautiful. It's set up like a Mediterranean hillside village with many small winding streets on the grounds. Walks were very nice, although some might find a leisurely walk a little arduous since it is so hilly. Near our building there was a waterfall in the cliff across the street. If you feel like a real hike you can actually meander your way into some open desert mountain terrain on the property. There are several pools on the property some with outdoor bars which were very nice, though drink prices were kind of steep (and mine were kind of weak). There are also several dining options on the property ranging from casual to upscale. I didn't actually try these places out except for some appetizers at one of the outdoor bars.There are also several well equipped gyms on the property too. The one I went to was expansive, had plenty of cardio, nautilus, and even an impressive array of free weights. It was probably around 1000 sq. feet, and I only ever saw one other person there. I may be mistaken, but I think you had to pay for gym access, but we were covered with my friend's travel rewards.Annoyingly, you had to pay for internet access which was hardwired with the outlet at the desk. This was about a year ago, so hopefully they have come into the modern age and put in wifi.Overall, I would definitely come back and highly recommend this place even though some of the costs are hidden.

<Author>SeattleRedBear
<Content>Views that go on forever I was here for five nights in early June attending a conference staying in two different rooms in the main building (first two nights by myself with a king bed and the remaining nights sharing a room with two double beds). I also visited the room of other colleagues in some of the other buildings. Pretty much identical layout for all standard rooms: living room (which included a sleeper sofa). short passage (with toilet/shower on one side and sink on the other) through to the bedroom. There are doors on either end of the passage so privacy can be had. As a standard room setup, this is great! Very comfortable beds. Flat panel TVs in both living room and bedroom. Wired internet in room. Lots of space. Good housekeeping.First, the positives. As other have commented, it is a beautiful location. There are pools throughout the property (so one never far away) and the main pool complex is enjoyable (although describing it as a water 'park' is a bit much...the highly advertised slide is a fun (but short) experience). The views from Different Point of View are stunning. I didn't eat there, but drinks on the terrace at night were very enjoyable. The grounds are immaculate. The staff are very friendly and a problem with our billing was fixed quickly by reception. When I called housekeeping about a missing bottle opener, staff brought the replacement within a couple minutes. They are also flexible about allowing you to stay after official checkout.As a meeting venue, it is fantastic. Event catering was good, the meeting rooms were configurable for different sizes of events and the AV setup was well-handled. The conference center is next to the main building, so very convenient for those staying in the main building.Now, the negatives. It is pretty isolated. The hotel does provide a shuttle (for a fee) to get to the local shopping mall, but you really need a car to get to anything outside of the resort. Without a car you are a willing hostage. Internet is $12/day (although you can print out boarding passes for free and they do offer free printing in the business center from your own laptop). As for the food, I only ate at the Cantina (the Mexican restaurant in the main building overlooking the family pool). it was OK but not great and I could taste no alcohol in my drinks (and IMO was overpriced for what you got). As others have noted, it is fairly spread out/hilly and for those with mobility issues, it can be a challenge. However, the free shuttle service is excellent (one of my colleagues was staying up the hill and the shuttle appeared 3 minutes after she placed the call) and the staff encourage use of the service. The layout is fairly confusing. There are a number of footpaths/bridges that provide shortcuts (so that guests don't have to walk in the roads) but they're not obvious. Again, staff are very good about telling you about them, but I think the signage to these paths could use some improvement. Signage for drivers was very good.I'm not a golfer, but friends that are commented on the great course and facilities available.

<Content>Lovely resort, very nice staff My sister and I stayed here for 3 nights at the beginning of May. The resort was lovely and really well kept, there were loads of pools dotted around (the Presidential pool is worth the walk, very quiet and secluded) and a few restaurants  bars to choose from. We were orginally allocated a room on the ground floor but I asked (at check-in) to be moved to a higher floor which was happily done for me. The rooms were spacious and comfortable, the bed was extremely comfortable! There was a member of staff called Gabriel on the front desk who was extremely helpful, giving us tips for things to do in the local area (Frank Lloyd Wright's house is recommeded) and also allowing us to use our room until late afternoon on the day we checked out. All in all the service was brilliant and resort lovely. It is quite spread out though so less abled people may find it a bit of a challenge getting around in the heat.

<Author>gvcrosby
<Content>Fun for the Family Overall, this was a nice hotel. We checked in late and the hotel was 100% full. As a result, we received a room in which the air conditioning didn't work. The hotel said they were unaware of the problem prior to our arrival and would fix it. They forgot to fix it. They did fix it on our second day at the property. They compensated us very well for the inconvenience!The room was nice, a very large 1 bedroom suite. Housekeeping didn't clean it very well after the prior guest, but they took care of that too.The facility was great for a family, lots of children's activities for my 5 year old son. He loved the waterslide, ping pong, tennis and hiking.Our stay was smack in the middle of their busy season, and it showed. The staff seemed overwhelmed, maybe even under-manned. However, EVERYONE we worked with was great. They were harried yet remained polite, professional, helpful, gracious and sympathetic when necessary! Any inconveniences we encountered were more than rectified by the staff!My son wants to go back and we are actually looking forward to it!

<Author>awaintroob
<Content>Great place to enjoy the outdoors Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs is built into the foothills in North Phoenix. It is right next to the Phoenix North Mountain Preserve so it is a wonderful location for hikers. The hotel has a waterpark with a 138 foot slide and lots of pools all over the property. The accommodations are very comfortable. I particularly liked the reading lights attached to the headboards on the bed on the side away from the bedside table. I also appreciated the availability of coin laundy machines. My 11 year old son loved the fact that there was always a pick-up basketball game on the basketball court. This is a great place to settle in to enjoy the Arizona outdoors. If the main focus of your trip is shopping or fine dining, you might want to stay closer to the bright lights of Scottsdale since north Phoenix doesn't offer much in the way of shopping or dining. One word of warning--this resort is built into a mountain so there's lots of ups and downs. It would be a tough place to manuever a child in a stroller or anyone with difficulty climbing or descending hills.

<Author>M&ALongGrove
<Content>~ Back Again! My wife and I spent a week at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs over New Year's break, 2008. We have been to the Phoenix/Scottsdale area many times, and have stayed at the Pointe a number of times before: winter and summer seasons.Needless to say, if we didn't like it, I wouldn't have booked this stay. However, I must say that having returned to the Pointe so often ~ probably 7 or 8 times, dating back 12 years ~ that we'll book someplace else, for our next visit.Remembering back to my first stay ~ a business trip ~ I was really impressed with the resort: unique grounds, great facilities, a nice selection of restaurants, fantastic pool area, comfortable and spacious rooms. I can tell you this: if you're a first-time visitor, you will probably love the place. After a couple business trips, I returned there a few times on my own, and actually got engaged at A Different Pointe of View, the upscale restaurant on the property. So, all things considered, the Pointe will always be special to me/us.On this most-recent visit, we used the Pointe as an home base. Aside from breakfast, we drove to other restaurants in the Phoenix/Scottsdale area to go the local route. As you know, it's always fun to try new restaurants, and go back to some local-area favorites. And there are plenty of great restaurants, not more than a 30-minute drive from the Pointe.If there was a negative Pointe on this trip, it would be the breakfast. We got the Hilton's Bounce Back Breakfast Deal. For a discounted price, you get to select from the breakfast menu every day. However, be careful here and read the fine print. To be fair, just about everything is included in the deal option; you can get a very inclusive breakfast everyday, including juice and coffee. But, read the menu closely. For example: one morning, my wife elected to order a breakfast entree that actually cost less than what I paid for the daily breakfast meal deal ~ you get coupons to use at the restaurant every day. Along with the entree, she ordered juice. Well, the entree she ordered did not include juice, so we got billed an extra $4.00. That rubbed me the wrong way. But those are the rules/terms, folks. So, read the fine print, or ask the waiter/waitress, before you order. Also, on this trip, a couple of the breakfasts came to us cool, not hot. Cool eggs. Hashed browns. Sausage/Bacon. It was just OK. I don't usually complain about minor things like this. However, it was sub-par, when expecting a nice, hot breakfast. Other than that . . .If you've never been to the Pointe, by all means, give it a try. If you're a young couple, it's a romantic place. If you have kids, the pool area is special, and there's a place to keep your kids, too. (Do everybody a favor, though. Keep them away from that young couple looking for a little romance!) There's something here for everybody to enjoy. Singles. Families. Young marrieds. Business travelers. Active older folks, too. First trip? You'll probably want to come back again. Like I said above, I did. We did. Now, for the time being . . .We'll leave the Pointe to you, . . . for a while.

<Author>DC_Runner78
<Content>Good location; Overall good experience Overall, we really enjoyed our stay at the Tapatio Cliffs. The location is nice -- close enough to interstate to be accessible, but far enough away that you feel like you're not in the midst of a metropolis. Across the street is a desert mountain preserve with trails, etc. that are good for hiking or running. The room was quite clean, although somewhat worn, especially the carpeting and some furniture. The rooms were probably originally built 30 years ago or so, so consequently have had some updating done. Our room had a balcony which was nice. Bathroom was fine as well. The water park and pools were nice, especially if you have kids. Although adults will love the bar service too! Had a pedicure at the spa -- the stylists were very accommodating and helpful. Food service is a little limited -- there is a very expensive Starbucks, a pool cafe, a pricey restaurant, and another restaurant that is more moderate...but you are close to other dining opportunities (driving distance, not walking distance) so it's not so much of a problem. I would definitely stay here again. Not sure if it's worth the $259 that I saw advertised on some websites (we used Hilton points), but it was a nice place in a good location with lots of amenities if you're willing to pay for them.

<Author>jcolem2000
<Content>Not a huge fan Just returned from a 5 day stay at the Tapatio Cliffs with a friend of mine on a golf weekend, and I will not be returning to this property.First of all, let me note that my friend is a Hilton Diamond member, and we used points for the room. If we had spent a lot of money I would have been really disappointed.The room itself was fine - since I was with a Diamond Member we received probably one of the nicest rooms in the complex - set far away from most of the craziness. If we had been put up in the main building or some of the more crowded areas I would have been very annoyed with the noise. Even up away from the crowds noise was still a problem, as was parking.The large pool was pretty much shut-down, very few people there and the waterslide they advertise with such fervor wasn't even in operation.The golf course messed up our reservations and moved our tee time an hour earlier without telling us. They claim they did not do this, but I had a reservation confirmation showing that they did. They moved our tee time to accommodate a larger group coming in, and didn't have the courtesy to call and let us know.The best part about our stay was the little pool up near our complex. It was quiet and relaxing. Although we had to call to the front desk to get the hot tub heater fixed (it was tepid at best), the maintenance person arrived promptly and fixed it.The worst part about the resort was the food. If you are going to charge ridiculous prices ($15 for a sandwich, $6 for a beer) - the food better be good. The food was terrible. Every meal we had at the resort was mediocre at best, and after the second day we just started leaving for our meals. Way over priced for what you get. We went out and bought a cooler for ourselves and kept beer and drinks on our balcony, and ate meals off-site - probably saved us a good $500 over the course of the week.Overall I will not return to this property - even using points for a free room I will most likely try to find another Hilton to use on my return.

<Author>MichWorldTraveler
<Content>A Very Unique Hotel One of the most unique hotels I've stayed at. The hotel is built into a mountain...And it's not all connected, the mountainside is adorned with dozens of buildings which make up the hotel rooms...All are outside access (the room door goes right to the outdoors, not a hallway), which I generally hate, but works well here. Big, comfortable rooms. One particular restaurant sticks out as 'AMAZING' to me--'A Different Pointe of View' has some of the most romantic views I've ever seen...It's at the top of the mountain, and you can see the entire Phoenix valley below. VERY COOL, VERY ROMANTIC. (And very expensive). Food and service isn't anything special, but it's worth it just for the views. If it's not summer and you can get one, get an outside table or a windowfront inside. Regardless, after dinner, go down a level to the outside bar for coctails to enjoy the view.

<Author>majorfoodie
<Content>Noisy, Noisy, Noisy!!! Never Again!!! They have taken an older, elegant property and painted it the most garish colors imaginable! The rooms are redone in a very haphazard way - they slapped on some paint but failed to refinish any of the wood items like the beat-up 70's era dressers. There is no refrigerator, so you are stuck hauling ice from another floor to keep any beverage cold. The worst complaint is that we asked for a quiet room - HAH! Right under our bedroom window, at 7am the workmen showed up and started hauling metal ladders out of the back of their trucks, yelling at each other, playing the radios in their trucks, and then the air compressor started and stayed on all day!!! When we complained, we were offered an even noisier room (instead of a suite) near the entrance - no upgrade, no discount, no free night. In addition, the highway just below is very noisy; because this is primarily a BUSINESS hotel, the guests themselves don't seem to realize that other people might be on VACATION so when they come back to their rooms drunk or get up at 6am they think it is perfectly OK to yell at their friends; they have outdoor meetings with loudspeakers that can be heard all over the property; and there is a riding academy by the golf course that smells like guess what? Horses! The beds were HARD - this was the upgraded mattress, at a time most hotel chains are changing to pillow-tops. And the pillows were so squishy I couldn't find enough of them to prop me up so I could read. Don't count on getting to eat at the fancy restaurant - it is booked by private parties most weekends and some week nights and is closed Sunday and Monday. The Mexican restaurant is a big joke - $12 for two American-style tacos! They have a captive audience and take full advantage of it.Because this resort is on a steep hillside, you either need to be in pretty good shape or ask for a shuttle everywhere you go. Won't be staying HERE again!

<Author>planningzone
<Content>Very Nice All-Suite Resort This resort was a welcome surprise. It was beautiful 20 years ago when I was in college, so I was a bit concerned that it could be very worn down. To my surprise, it was in great shape. It was very obvious that the rooms had been refurbished. My wife LOVED it and wanted to stay a couple extra nights. It was closed when we were there, because it was cold out, but they had a sign in front of the slide saying that you can ask the bartender to turn it on if you want to use it. I thought that was pretty cool.You can drive and park in front of your room. If you get there in the day-time there is plenty of room-front parking, so you will not need the bellman to help you. If you arrive at night, GET THE BELLMAN'S HELP! This is because the parking is very crowed at night and you probably need to park away from your room and walk. I was there on a weekend and at night parking was VERY crowded. I guess you can take a drive to the room to see if you can find a good spot and return for help if it does not pan-out...??There is no short-term parking, so either there is a spot or there isn't. The streets are VERY narrow, so if you try to double park and unload, you will block the entire street.I will be going back for sure!

<Author>RodeTripp
<Content>Renovations.......Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort Having previously stayed at Tapatio Cliffs on numerous occassions, I was somewhat disappointed with the recent renovations. The many buildings which comprise the resort used to be white. With the red tile roofs and lush vegetation, it was stunning in appearance and reminicient of a tropical villa on a hillside. The buildings have now been repainted in somewhat bold colors (mustard, red, brown etc.) The walkways between the buildings have also been painted in these colors but not the same color as any of the buildings they connect. The result, a look which reminds of the barrios bajos (slums) of Mexico City.As for the rooms, ours was many shades of avocado green with some yellow. It is unfortunate that avocato was chosen as the new color to represent this southwestern venue. It was also disturbing that the new couch was already ripped and that the new cocktail and end tables had brown cardboard glued to them in various places (packing materials which are stuck to the metal frames).For a once wonderful resort, the aesthetics now leave much to be desired.

<Content>Disappointing Service, Adequate Room, Great Amenities I have stayed at this resort three times; I'd expect my most recent visit will be my last, though my overall fondness for the Hilton amenities might override my disappointment with the poor service I experienced recently.Problems: at check-in, I requested a change from the non-smoking room I had reserved on the Hilton Web site to a smoking room, as my non-smoking traveling companion chose to stay elsewhere. I arrived at my (somewhat hard-to-find) room, weary from a very long flight, only to discover that it was a non-smoking room despite my request. I called the front desk and was told that I could move right next door (to a room that was similar, though slightly less desirable), but when I moved into the new room I discovered it was also non-smoking. I called the desk and was told to go ahead and smoke in that room; they would bring an ashtray.Additional problems: I departed from my room on Sunday at about 11 a.m. and returned around 10 p.m., only to discover that the room had not been cleaned. I called the guest hotline and was told that it was too late to have the room cleaned but that I could have fresh towels and coffee; when I inquired about the reason the room was not cleaned, I was transferred (without further assistance or apology) to the front desk. The front desk personnel stated I must have left the do not disturb sign on the door (I hadn't!) and offered to have the room cleaned immediately, but as I was ready to sleep I declined the offer in favor of the fresh towels and coffee alone. (They arrived within about 15 minutes.) I never received any explanation, apology, or adjustment. An additional disappointing feature was the $13.95 per day fee for internet access (with VPN), essential for staying connected with work while I visited Phoenix for a family emergency. It worked well and was easy to set up, but free wireless access would seem to be an expected amenity at a hotel of this type.The hotel setting is attractive, with views of mountains and city lights. (Warning: for some rooms, one is faced with a very steep walk to/from the only parking options.) The suite was comfortable--and, as usual, the beds, linens, and toiletries were perfect. This room was far less luxurious than the two others I had experienced at this hotel, though. Housekeeping (when offered!) was excellent, and the room was very clean. I liked the two-room arrangement and the flat-screen televisions in each. The AAA rate on the Hilton site was great.It's too bad the service was dreadful. From a hotel of this type, I'd expect much better--and, from my experience, it's possible to find great service at comparable locations in the Phoenix area.

<Author>Schmengi9
<Content>Nice little getaway We stayed at the Tapatio Cliffs resort for one night after Christmas as a getaway from the family and it was very worthwhile overall. We called ahead to ask for and received an early check-in, which allowed us additional time to make use of some of the resorts' facilities. This was a very nice touch, since check-in is usually at 4 PM, which limits how much you can enjoy a place on a one-night stay.We thought the room was quite spacious and clean overall, with warm, yet modern decorative finishes. The bed was wonderful. There was only one vanity for the bathroom, which was located across a hallway from the water closet itself. The light switch for the water closet was on the outside wall, which was little awkward. The separate living room was fine, but the sofa was stiff and there was no coffee table to set a drink on. It would also have been helpful for the room to have a refrigerator separate from the mini-bar like some other resorts have been known to provide. (We'd heard mixed reviews about the Different Point of View Restaurant and decided instead to stay in with food  wine from the AJ's Fine Foods store located north of the resort at 7th St.  Thunderbird, which was an excellent store and turned out to be an excellent choice! No fridge meant meant creative use of the sink and ice bucket for our wine, cheese and sushi. Ce la vie!)Although it was in the 50s-low 60s the day we stayed at TC, we decided that it was still worth a trip to the water park/ pool. (When you come from the 10s  20s, 50s  60s is quite a warm-up!) This area is pretty well removed from the vast majority of the guest rooms and almost needs to be driven to because of the lack of walks along most of the interior drives. The pool facilities were very nice and very welcomed and the Cascades bar was also good. There is a smaller pool/ spa/ workout room in the center of the main guest room area, though it looked largely closed while we were there.One area I would caution guests to was the Point in Tyme restaurant, which is located near the main pool area. We went for breakfast before checking out and it was a disaster. The service was abysmal and the food neither worth the wait or the price (45 minutes and $13 for huevos rancheros!). This was noteworthy because it was definitely not high season when we were there, so I can only imagine what a treat it is in peak times.Overall, I would recommend a stay at Tapatio Cliffs. My wife and I would definitely have stayed another night if our schedule would have allowed and hope to get back for another stay the next time we're in Phoenix. I should note that the resort is in the final stages of a renovation project, which currently has the main lobby gutted and moved to temporary quarters elsewhere in the main building. Some of the parking around the main building was torn up or used as staging, but it wasn't a big deal overall and I wouldn't let it dissuade you from staying at the TC.

<Author>TravelFan
<Content>Quiet Christmas Stay We stayed at the Point Hilton Tapitio for six days over Christmas 2007. The property is undergoing a complete renovation. The lobby/check-in has been temporarily moved across the street to the ballroom. They were repaving the roads when we arrived so they placed us in the main building, which is a four story garden type hotel. We were on the third floor overlooking one of the pools. When you enter your suite, there is a sitting room with a desk, couch, bar, and a new flat panel tv. Then you walk into a tiled area that has a sink, counter, mirror, and a separate room for the shower/tub and restroom. Two people can easily get ready at the same time in this arrangement. The final room of the suite is the bedroom. Ours came with two queen beds, both with plush down comforters and pillows. This room also had a tv, a closet, and a chest of drawers. I believe each room also has a balcony. The couch in the sitting room did not make out into a bed, so the following day, we asked if we could move to one of their outer buildings. They were very gracious to move us into building one. In our new room, the couch made out into a bed, so the room could accommodate up to a maximum of six people, although we just had four. The views from the balcony are a lot prettier from the outer buildings, although the parking can be a bit challenging. (There are narrow roads between the buildings which has limited parking for guests. If you get there later in the evening and the spaces are full, you have to walk up or down the hill to a parking lot). The hotel was very quiet during the Christmas season, and they were not using many of their outer buildings. The hotel staff was very accommodating, meeting every request we had. They give complimentary papers in the morning. They have a computer where you can check in for your flight if you are flying. There are many pools across this property, a work out room, golf, many restaurants, and hiking and horse-back riding right next door to the property. We did not get to take advantage of all of the amenities since we were visiting family, but the room was perfect for our Christmas stay. The staff is to be commended for their excellent service.

<Author>Gracie99uk
<Content>Nice pools but lacking in customer service! We just spent two nights at this Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs. We're Hilton Gold members and were disappointed not to receive any acknowledgement of this at check-in. Infact we didn't really receive any welcome at all. Check-in agent just gave us keys and a map and told us where to go. Disappointed with room on level two near adult pool - on entering it was very dark and smelt funny. Shower pressure was good however and bed comfy. Woke up after first night with Hilton breakfast coupons under the door with letter acknowledging gold status ... would have been appreciated if we hadn't booked room rate with breakfast included!!!!If you want to relax by the pool then this hotel is okay. The adult pool is next to the hotel's mexican restaurant and you can swim up to the bar and order bar food and drinks. We ate burger and fries and chicken tacos at lunch ... burger was fine but the shredded chicken taco was a bit hit and miss! The best pools are at the falls village.There are two large pools and a slide (fun) and a bar area with food available. The loungers at the adult pool are cushioned and really comfortable whereas the loungers at the falls aren't as comfy! Our biggest complaint with this hotel is the attitude of staff. With the exception of housekeeping who always greeted us with a smile and hello no-else seemed to want to be there. Check-in were just awful, bar staff fairly miserable and our waitress at breakfast was disinterested ... we waited a while for her to reappear when we had finished but she was a no show so in the end we just left our breakfast vouchers and a tip on the table and just left.Other than lunch at the pool we didn't eat at the hotel. There are lots of restaurant choices nearby as well as the Outlet Mall at Anthemif you're interested in shopping!!!!

Of course I have to admit that the vacation traveler is what this hotel was intended for. However, they have many conference rooms and business rooms for meetings and I am sure they get plenty of complaints from business travelers.

<Author>JChapma
<Content>Great, Relaxing get away My wife and I stayed at the Tapatio Cliffs Hilton the last week of August, and had a really great experience. We arrived on a Thursday night, and were immediately impressed with how friendly everyone was. We checked in quickly (HHonors), and were driven up the hill to our room. When the sun came up the next day, we realized we had been driven about 400 yards, so it's definitely walkable without luggage. We had a very nice two room suite next to the presidential pool; clean and well cared forThis hotel has a lot of choices for entertainment with 7 pools, and we spent a lot of our time at the pool all by ourselves. It was really, really relaxing. The fitness center is nice and does have a fairly decent selection of free weights. We hiked every morning from the hotel and there are a couple of different trails to choose from, although they're not extremely isolated (you're in metro Phoenix, so we expected as much). Going left under the highway led to better trails. We only ate dinner at the hotel one night; at the Casades (since it's casual). They have Mexican food. It was ok, but we had a great Tex Mex meal 5 minutes away Sierra Bonita restaurant. The bellman recommended it, and it was a really good choice.

<Author>suzansmile
<Content>Look elsewhere for a place to stay My friends and I, from a local mom's club, decided to stay at The Pointe, for our bi-yearly mom's night away. All of us are mom of young children and we were looking forward to being away from our families, spending quality time together and sleeping in the next day. When my friend and I checked into our room, we noticed that the bed skirt on my bed was filthy. The bed skirt on my friend's bed was splattered with blood (without a doubt) and I also found that I had a dead bug between my cover and sheets. We phoned the front desk and housekeeping was dispatched and the bedding was replaced. For dinner we went to The Pointe In Tyme. Our waiter was very personable, he offered suggestions and raved over the onion soup. Our drink order was taken and 12 minutes later, our drinks arrived. Our meal, consisting of 2 burgers, 2 soups and 3 salads arrived 40+ minutes later. The soup was horrible. Grocery store, off the shelf soup has more flavor and personality then what we were served. The pecan salads were the size of a side salad. They consisted of greens, pecans and with very little cheese. Though it was very tasty, they were certainly not worth the $8.00 price tag. We informed the waiter that the soup certainly did not live up to our expectations. The waiter tasted my soup and confirmed that it was very bland and was probably a pot thrown together, after they had run out of the earlier batch. We were offered a free desert and the cost of the soups were removed from our bill. After a disappointing meal, we retired to our rooms. Sunday morning, yes SUNDAY morning before 9 am, we were woken by the hammering, chiseling, tape ripping and talking going on while the removal of room numbers and application of new ones took place, to our door and the rooms around us. This was not the only project going on. I phoned the manager and was informed that he was not available and he would be calling me back. I did let the desk know what my complaint was and within 10 minutes, the one project (chiseling the numbers off the door) was stopped but there were still other work going on that we could hear. At 10:30 am, my friend and I went to take showers and found there was no running water. I phoned the front desk and was notified that the city had a station down. We were able to bathe and dress in our friend's room, located in another building.Overall, I can forget about the bug (we live in AZ) and the issue with the water, BUT will not consider staying at this resort again. The filth in the room and the lack of consideration of their guests comfort, is incomprehensible. In the end, I was offered a voucher, for a night at the resort, at a later date. I was told that since I had prepaid, I could not have a refund. I did insist on a refund, and was informed I would receive a check in a few weeks.. My friends and I plan on sharing this experience with our friends, family and business associates.

<Author>jo-tris
<Content>Ok, but won't be going back... Stayed at the Tapatio for our summer family vacation. Our all-suite accommodation was just okay, and rather cramped for 2 teenagers and 2 adults. The sofa bed consisted of a piece of something they called a mattress that was VERY uncomfortable, slept the rest of the time on just the sofa itself. No refrigerator in the room, only a min-bar so needless to say, we spent over $35 on bar items. Our first day, the toilet in our room got clogged but maintenance quickly took care of the problem. Room service was always prompt and pretty decent. We chose the Tapatio based on reviews on TripAdvisor and the hotel's website. Let me just say, the hotel is NOT as nice as it appears or claims to be on the website. The Falls Water Village offers acres of pools... yes, there are pools scattered throughout the property but nothing special. The main pool area has 2 pools, lots of lounge chairs, a bar, and one pathetic little water slide, so the hype on the website is very misleading. The website also stated that they have a lap pool, upon check-in no one knew anything about a lap pool when asked, in fact management came out and specifically said that they do not have a lap pool, but we later found an area in the main pool that was designated for lap swimming, of sorts. We ate once at a Pointe in Thyme - save your money and eat somewhere else. The food was ok, service good, but overpriced. We also made the mistake of eating at La Cantina, horrible. The hotel is about 20 years old and is showing signs of wear and tear and is in desperate need of renovation. The fitness centre is small and the equipment is old. Overall it wasn't a horrible stay but for the price and with other hotel options in Phoenix, we'll stay elsewhere next time.

<Author>RedSox604
<Content>Fantastic, Relaxing weeklong visit Stayed here a week in June, for the Red Sox series in Phoenix and just a girls getaway weekend. We had a great and very relaxing stay at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs.I wasn't expecting much, after the registration clerk who checked me in very late Wednesday night was not very friendly or informative, but everything was great thereafter. It is a bit overwhelming at first, seeing the layout and many buildings that are mostly up on the hillside, but the very friendly bellman gave me a map and directions to my room, and I found it with ease.THE SUITES:-All rooms are two room suites: a living room area with wetbar, bedroom, and bathroom with a separated sink area. There was also a balcony with chairs/table to enjoy the view.-The beds were very comfortable, the regular Hilton Serenity bedding type.-The room was very clean, as were the linens and towels. The towels were also a bit more substantial that a standard hotel bath towel.-Bathrobes provided for your use during stay.-Plenty of closet space and drawers to unpack your belongings.-Fairly soundproof: I didn't hear much noise from the adjacent suites, except one evening when a child was crying fairly loud.-Drawback, is that there is no in-room safe for storing belongings.RECREATION:-7 pools total: the large Falls Water Village, which featured two pools, waterfalls, activities, etc., as well as smaller/quieter pools scattered throughout the property. The smaller pools had nice padded lounge chairs, which were a plus.-Ability to reserve a poolside cabana at the Falls Water Village. At around $50 for the day, well worth it. It was sometimes difficult to find enough shade at the regular chairs. The cabana gets you two padded lounge chairs, table and chairs, ceiling fan, mini-fridge and TV.-Poolside service at the Falls Water Village, including food and a full bar. Just raise the flag on your lounge chair and they will stop by for your order. Someone will also come by about once an hour and provide you with an ice cold towel to cool down.DINING:-Enjoyed a late lunch at the Pointe in Tyme restaurant. The service was excellent, and although we ordered only sandwiches and french fries, they were really excellent.-Had room service a couple of times: typical of hotel room service. The menu was similar to Pointe in Tyme, and the food was good, but not as great as it was at the restaurant. They were very prompt, and after waiting only 35 minutes for dinner one evening, the called to offer apologies and brought complimentary dessert (which was excellent!)-Food ordered poolside is provided by the Cascades. It was OK(since I didn't need to leave my cabana), but I've had much better. However the margaritas are excellent.-Coffee, lattes, breakfast pastries and fruit are offered all day in the gift shop. Nice to stop in for a quick latte or snack.-I didn't get an opportunity to try The Cantina: tried one evening, but despite seeing several empty tables, was informed by the hostess that it would be a 45 minute wait. OTHER:Service- The front desk staff and the concierge were not particularly friendly or helpful. The rest of the staff: waiters, bellman, bartenders, etc., were very accomodating.Location- Easy to find, about a 15 minute drive from Sky Harbor airport. Not much within walking distance given the size of the resort, so you will likely need a car to get anywhere outside the resort. There is a Starbucks within a 1/2 mile of the resort entrance, and Scottsdale is an easy drive for finding dining and shopping options.Housekeeping-They did a great job each day, and were quiet while they went about it. I slept in every morning, and wasn't awoken by the sounds of nearby rooms being cleaned.Parking-Not enough parking at the buildings up on the hills. Each building easily had 20-30 Suites, but only 6-8 parking spaces. Since everything is on hills, it can be quite a hike up to your suite if you have parked nearer the main building. View-I paid extra for an upgraded view ($5 based on availability via the hotel's website). I think in some cases, the view from a standard room's balcony would literally be of the back of another building.Business-Just a quick note, since on my last review of a Hilton I noted that their internet charges were excessive, this Hilton also charges for internet use in the room, or $0.49/minute in the business center BUT at least this Hilton lets you print boarding passes for free.Overall - my friend and I really enjoyed our stay at the Pointe Hilton. It was just right for a girls weekend away. If I visit the area again, I will certainly consider staying at this resort.  
<Date>Jun 13, 2007

<Author>MrsBerry
<Content>Great views of Phoenix My husband and I stayed at this Hilton 5/31-6/5/2007. The hotel is located about 20 minutes from the airport and we found it convenient to everything. Upon driving up, a very friendly bellman met us and showed us where to check in. We were given a room in the mountainside suites. The hotel property is laid out up a cliff, so very spread out. I would not agree with the person who said to park first, then check in. Unless you are in the main building, you will need to drive to your room as many are on the cliff. Our room was in building 21 on the fourth floor. It was conveniently located near the work out center and another small pool. We liked the area as it was quiet with great views of Phoenix. The suite was fine with a nice balcony. There is some deferred maintenance in the room and around the property. Nothing drastic or anything that bothered us. We are Hilton Honors Gold members and got breakfast coupons toward the buffet. The coupon covers a continental buffet of yogurt, assorted pastries  fruit. For another $4 you can add omelets, bacon, frech toast, etc. It was a great breakfast buffet! (the bacon was fabulous!!) The pools were nice with cool water and a whirlpool with warm (not hot) water. We thought both were kept at a nice temperature. The concierge recommended a fabulous Mexican restaurant nearby called Via delosSantos. We ate there 3 of our 4 nights in Phoenix. It was delicious! Try the calabacita fajitas. YUMMY!! We would recommend this nice 4 star hotel.

<Author>Okaye
<Content>Great Girls Getaway I spent a long weekend in March at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio with two former college roommates, and the hotel was perfect for us. After straightening out a mishap at check-in (we opened the door to our room to find it was already occupied), we got an even better room. The double room with the sleeper sofa worked great for us. The room seemed to have been recently redecorated and although there were a few signs of wear, everthing was fresh and clean.The grounds are pretty, with different buildings set into the cliffs across the property. We found the staff to be friendly and very accommodating. We loved that they have an adult pool, and spent time by it in the evening when we wanted to relax and talk without any screaming and splashing in the background. We would have liked to try the bar  restaurant at the top of the property, but there were special events going on there each night so we didn't have that opportunity. We would certainly stay here again if we return to the Phoenix area!

<Author>OOBDC
<Content>Enjoyable Stay - Lots of potential downside I stayed at the Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort for three nights in mid April. My wife and I had a wonderful time, but we did stay on Hilton Honors Reward Points. I am not sure I would鈥檝e had as wonderful a time if I was paying. While physically beautiful, the property is very hilly; so if you have issues with walking and/or dealing with up/down hill grades, this property will be a challenge. Parking on the resort is tough. There are not enough spots near the various resort room buildings for all the guests鈥?cars. We did not have any issues with this except for the one night we returned to the resort late at night. We ended parking quite a ways from our room building. Smoking. The resort rooms are non smoking, but guests smoke on the decks and patios outside the rooms. There鈥檚 nothing you can do about this except complain, and nothing will happen. If you do not like cigarette smoke and you end up in a room above or next to a room where people are smoking on the decks/patios you will be upset. The lounge at the Different Point of View is all smoking. They have a decent jazz band there on Friday and Saturday nights and the view from the patios outside are very nice. But, if you do not like cigarette smoke, your visit to the lounge may not be enjoyable. We got lucky and sat in area where no one was smoking, but there were ashtrays on every table. Breakfast and brunch service in the Pointe in Tyme dining room was very slow. We were told that if we wanted something off the menu, the wait would be an hour. We opted for the satisfactory buffet. Our room was quiet, except for one instance of kids yelling in the Cabana Circle pool later at night. The resort is pretty and is well maintained. The one meal we ate in the Different Point of View Lounge was tasty (and again, we were lucky and not bothered smokers). The Different Point of View Lounge has the same menu as the Restaurant but seating is first come first served. On the Saturday night during out stay, there was a high school prom on the property. We not impacted by this event, but my wife overheard a property staffer tell two prom goers (presumably the two in charge of the event), that if there were any problems, the whole thing would be shut down. We enjoyed ourselves but there are numerous chances for a stay here to turn bad, in my opinion.

<Author>h24
<Content>Wonderful Mini-Honeymoon My husband and I were married on March 10 in Tempe (at his mother's house) and were going to stay that night at the Pointe South Mountain but the day before he discovered he could have another day off from work and when I called the PSM to add another night they told me the rate would be double for the second night because of higher occupancy. I only had dial up at my future mother in law's house so it was hard for me to do any sort of detailed search for a hotel. I stumbled upon some details about Tapatio Cliffs and called their reservation line to put us down for two nights. I called PSM to cancel and the rep tried to tell me if I called on March 10th I might be able to add the second night at a lower rate if they had an opening (what part of it is our wedding weekend didn't they understand?). I mention all of this because I was worried at this point that my experience with PSM did not bode well for our alternate arrangements. How wrong I was!Staying at the Tapatio Cliffs was wonderful! When we arrived to check in we let the person at the desk know we'd just gotten married (I think the fact that I still had my hair up helped) and he said he would upgrade us from a basic room to an executive one. He also had chocolate covered strawberries and champagne sent up that night with handwritten note of congratulations.The room was lovely, it overlooked one of the many pool areas and it had a bedroom separate from the living room. A tv was in both rooms. The bed was extra comfy and we were at the end of a hall so it was very quiet. Room service was fairly priced and the food was wonderful. While we were there we had cheese pizza, veggie burgers with fries, creme brulee, and as many pitchers of ice water as we wanted. The next morning we ate a breakfast buffet (I had opted for rooms that included some romance package deals like breakfast buffets for two and a buy one get one free entree coupon -- really worth it). The fruit was fresh and the service was wonderful.Later that day we sat by the pool and ordered drinks -- they have flags on the chairs so you can put them up to let staff know you'd like to order something. I'd never done anything like this before so it felt very decadent. The pools were great, we even tried out the water slide. The music selection playing by the pool was good too, a fair mix of old and new top-40 songs. We ate at the Mexican restaurant they have on site and again, the service and food were excellent. I know I read gushing reviews and think things couldn't have possibly been that great but they really were. Well, here are a few critical comments. It was weird was how far away the ice machine was on our floor but we just ordered pitchers of ice water instead. I will also add that you might want to map the location of the hotel because we were happy to be away from it all so I don't know about how close off-site dining or activities are.We did have an experience that could be viewed as negative as on our first night there we had a knock on the door and a plumber said he needed to check the bathtub because he thought it was leaking downstairs. We were kind of annoyed to be intruded upon especially when the gentleman checked the tub and said he'd come back tomorrow morning. My husband asked if we could call and let the front desk know when we were up and about and they could come then and the plumber agreed. The next day we called to let them know we were heading to the pool and when we came back there was a note saying everything was okay. The man was professional and we both felt that it did not ruin our experience at the hotel. There was a moment of panic, however, when we asked if we'd have to move rooms and were told the hotel was entirely booked. Luckily we were able to stay and had a great weekend.We actually live in Las Vegas so we're used to seeing fancy resort hotels but I loved the atmosphere of Tapatio Cliffs. And to be away from the smoke, gambling, and crowds was great too. The service was great and the food everywhere on site was top notch. They really seemed to care about our experience and wanted to help us make it a special weekend.Totally worth it!

<Author>JLC&N
<Content>Really nice stay this time I've stayed here before and had a less pleasurable experience due to the noise of the main building. The hotel is divided up into separate areas of buildings, each with it's own little pool and amenities.This time, I requested a quiet room and was accommodated. We were put in the Canyon View suites which are located well above the main hotel. This area has it's own pool, jacuzzi, pizza deli and the gym. We were against the rock mountain and on the top floor, which made it a quiet, enjoyable experience. We watched the sunset over the desert from our balcony. We did venture down to the main pool and water slide so my son could play, however, even he preferred the restful solitude of the pool in our area. The little pizza deli is right off the pool and has drinks, pizza, ice cream and sandwiches. It stays open pretty late too.The on-site restaurants seem nice but expensive. We drove down the hill (North) on 7th and dined at other restaurants in the area. There is a Starbucks just a half a mile North of the hotel, down the hill, on the West side of 7th, for coffee junkies like me. Lots of fast food on N. 7th as well as a few little cafes and chain restaurants. If you go South on 7th the neighborhood is a little rough.If you have any difficulties walking, the hillside suites are not the place for you. Rooms are literally in the side of a mountain and while there is a shuttle, it's still a walk to wherever you want to go.Our room was well appointed, the beds were comfortable and the linens and toiletries very nice. Resort gounds are very pretty and staff is friendly and accommodating. I had a government rate which was very good. We will stay here again.

<Author>jstjumpin
<Content>Hilton misses the mark I have to say that Hilton missed the mark again. I was actually excited to come to this resort after reading the reviews here because I really don't have any confidence in the Hilton brand. I believe they are masters at puffing the goods. It seems that many of the Hilton properties are touted as being the best and when you arrive, you are always short changed. This property didn't differ.I came to this property for a business function. Prior to arrival, I was concerned that I receive a quality room due to the many comments about the rooms being dated. I was assured I would receive a great room and upon arrival, I recieved a room with a view of the adjacent highway. HINT: When a customer takes the time to call prior to arrival, you have a small idea they might be a tad bit high maintenance. A note in the file and a proper room assignment might have been a good idea on their part, but this is absolutely typical of the Hilton brand. Of course I requested a move and only when pushed did the staff offer me a pool view for an upcharge of $50. The staff assumed that because there was an upcharge, I wouldn't pay it. How ridiculous! I accepted the upcharge and was happy to have a better view. The room was spacious and fairly well appointed. I would agree it was dated, but according to the staff it IS remodeled. They did a remodel about 4 years ago on the entire property, so what you see is what you get.During my stay, we ran out of toilet paper. We had to request this from the staff FOUR times. This was ridiculous given that we had put the empty roll out for the housekeeping staff to see. There were other occasions where I needed to call the front desk (usually to request toilet paper) and found they did not answer the phone. I needed to know what time my event started and was quoted a wrong time which caused me to arrive late. I needed to know what time check out was an had to call three times before someone answered. The pool was lovely, the staff were friendly and helpful and provided great service. The property is full of hills (it sits on the side of a cliff) but I didn't mind that. I found a very private pool w/ hot tub called the Hidden Valley pool that was very enjoyable and I never saw another soul there.The property needs maintenance and again I feel they missed the mark in using red, green, yellow and blue lighting all over the property which gives you a sense you might have been transported to the Circus. The Cabannas are a joke - don't waste your time or money. There are small touches everywhere that reflect Hilton's lack of attention to detail which will cause this this frequent traveler to continue to AVOID the Hilton Brand.

<Content>A Peaceful Stay Received this hotel from Priceline when I bid $75 on resort in Phoenix North. It was a Sunday night, and the resort did not feel crowded to me. I was traveling with my 74 year old mother and requested a handicapped suite with two queens. We were on the top floor of the main building. The unit was massive - a large bedroom and a huge sitting area. Mom loved the handicapped shower. We enjoyed having two TVs. There were two robes for our use. We also liked the little extras - like cotton balls  q-tips in the bathroom. Broadband is wired in the rooms, and costs $11.95/24hours, but I got lucky in that the last occupant had apparently bought internet late the previous night, and I had free broadband all evening. Staff was efficient, Marion the concierge was helpful, bell desk was very friendly, and the workout room was very nice, with lots of top-notch Precor equipment. The hotel could use some updating, but otherwise it was great.

<Author>tboyerpa
<Content>Very Good Value for Families Hilton Tapatio is a very good property for families looking for a fun vacation in the sun. We (my wife, myself and two daughters 5  9) just returned from a four day stay 4/10 - 4/13 and had an excellent experience.This resort is a solid 3 - 3 1/2 stars and a good overall value but do not book expecting a 4 or 5 star property. For the $150/night we paid, I was very happy.All rooms are two room suites with a good layout, comfortable beds and furnishings. The furnishings and room were that of a quality 3 - 3 1/2 star hotel. Very nice and functional, not the bells, whistles and special touches of a 4 or 5 star resort.The Falls Water Village has 2 large pools, waterslide, 2 hot tubs, bathrooms and pool side service. While the pool area did get crowded, we were always able to find 4 lounge chairs together and the crowds didn't bother us. Basically families with younger children splashing and laughing in the water. The resort has a total of 8 pools (some very small) and the pools outside of the Falls Water Village seemed more quiet, sedate and an adult setting. They do have some pools reserved for Adults Only.The pool towels were a bit thin, but we got two a piece and that worked just fine. We found the pool area well maintained and the pool bathrooms some of the cleanest I have ever found. The pool side service was very good and responsive. Just raise the flag on your chair and they were by to assist within a minute or two.Overall, Hilton Tapatio is a very nice property for a reasonable price. If you want 4-5 stars, luxury at every turn and a quite pool area, this is not the property for you.If you are looking for a quality spot with very good pool offerings and a reasonable price (vs. $250 + for a higher rated hotel), then you can't go wrong at Tapatio Cliffs.
