<Author>fastrunningmom
<Content>Fine but not worth a special trip We flew into Phoenix to go to Sedona and the Grand Canyon. We weren't sure where to stay in Phoenix, so looked on Tripadvisor for help. I wanted a great pool for my two kids, and decided to split our time in Phoenix between Tapatio Cliffs and the Pointe South Mountain Resort.Tapatio Cliffs is an attractive hotel built on a cliff. There are many pools, the most popular for kids being the Falls complex, with one good water slide, an irregular shaped pool with plenty of play space and a jacuzzi. It was nice, but not spectacular. The rooms were clean and well decorated. I don't like though, having the toilet and tub in a separate area from the sink. It seems crazy to have a hall between them, but oh well. The suite also has a sitting area with a TV, then you pass through the hall with the bathroom facilities into a bedroom, nicely furnished. There is a small fridge in the suite with freezer, and two TV's - one in the sitiing area and one in the bedroom. This was nice for me as I could put the kids to sleep and still read or watch TV in the sitting room.The onsite restaurants were good, but pricey.To be honest, if I returned to Phoenix I would stay at the Pointe South Mountain resort instead, as their pool complex is much much bigger, better and more fun. The Falls pool complex at Tapatio Cliffs is OK, but might bore kids after a day or two.

<Content>Drenched in Sun and Beauty Congratutlations to Hilton !!! This resort is another example of why I can count on the Hilton Brand. This resort is a high end four star resort. Tip: Make sure to always check the temps and weather in Sedona before leaving Phoenix. Climbing up to 4,400 feet can provide a few surprises. We experienced cold and wet weather after having just leaving Phoenix and a two hour drive. This resort is loaded with pools and fun things to do. Take the mountain hike for great views of the region. Have fun and enjoy ! We did and will return soon.

<Author>MyTravelLog
<Content>Great Place to Stay I stayed at Tapatio Cliffs while attending a conference at the resort earlier this month. The front desk staff was courteous and check-in was a breeze. I was actually able to check-in earlier than the normal time. Although the grounds are immaculate, they can be difficult to navigate; however, the hotel does offer shuttle service to get around the complex. The hotel isn't situated close to anything so I would highly recommend renting a car during your stay. Although not widely advertised, the hotel does shuttle guests to the mall (the shuttle leaves at 11:30am and returns around 3:30pm). I dined at the Different Pointe of View restaurant which was fabulous with a view to die for. Reservations are recommended especially if dining around sunset. Keep in mind that this restaurant isn't for the budget minded diner. There is also a lounge on the first level with live entertainment. I also ate at the Pointe in Tyme restaurant which had great food at a reasonable price. All in all I truly enjoyed my stay.

<Author>whosyer12
<Content>Exceptional! Took a Spring Training break from March 11-14, 2007 and was lucky enough to draw this resort on a very reasonable Priceline bid. It is a beautiful place and the grounds and all common areas are meticulously maintained. The two room suite was very nice and comfortable and clean. We were in the Mountainside area and our balcony overlooked a beautiful, lightly used pool and whirlpool. We had an early flight in and arrived at the hotel at 9:30AM. To my amazement we were allowed to check in immediately!. We had a late flight out on departure day so the day before I called the front desk and asked for a two hour late check out. They advised that they were at capacity and politely declined. Later that evening I went to the lobby to print our boarding passes (free, in the business center) and stopped by the front desk and made my late check-out request again. They immediately and graciously granted a 2:00PM checkout. I guess the point here would be: if you have a reasonable request that is declined--ask again on a different shift OR make your request in person. We didn't dine at the hotel other than a decent, reasonably (comparatively speaking, given the surroundings) priced room service breakfast. There are several very casual decent dining choices at the intersection about two minutes north of the hotel.Only a couple slight negatives:--In our building noise was a slight factor. We didn't hear other voices, but could hear doors slamming, etc, and the plumbing was moderately noisy.-- As others have pointed out, the entire property is quite hilly which makes the atmosphere of the place. I really can't see, however, how only but the most fit of older seniors could consider staying here.We loved this place. Would even consider paying other than a Priceline rate (gasp!) to stay here again.

<Author>tripmomSanDiego
<Content>Definitely recommend After a long drive, we arrived at the hotel about 11 pm and were quickly checked in by the staff. Some reviews stated that parking was a problem. We never found that to be the case during our 2 night stay. Parking fills up in the parallel spots right in front of the rooms, but large parking lots are on the other side of the rooms. Our room was a 1 bedroom suite w/balcony. We found it large and nicely decorated. We found the seperate living room and bathroom areas a nice touch especially since our child gets up at the crack of dawn. One parent could get up and play with him in the other room with the door closed and let the other parent get more sleep. The room was very clean except the floors. I think they could have vaccumed and swept better. I found the plumbing in the room above us to be very loud in the early morning. We did not need an alarm clock because every time someone went the bathroom upstairs it jarred us awake at 6am. The noise shut off after 30 seconds or so but by then my child was already awake for the day. This was my only major complaint about the hotel. Other than that everything else was better that I had expected. The view from our room balcony was very nice and we overlooked the waterfall which sounded nice as well.We spent sometime at a few of the pool areas and were thrilled at how much thought had gone into the design. There are many water features such as water fountains and waterfalls. The pool closes at 7pm. We thought that was early compared to other hotels we have been to in the past.We had a late breakfast at the Point in Thyme restaurant on the grounds. We found it to have a nice atmosphere. A buffet is offered or you can order from a menu. I was not expecting much based off of previous reviews so I was pleasantly surprised at the taste and quality of the food we ordered. The staff seemed to go out of their way to make my child happy without any requests from us. He ordered the Mickey Mouse pancake breakfast. The meal came out with the pancakes decorated with fresh fruit. The costs of the meal was only a few dollars more than we would have paid at a breakfast chain restaurant.We came back from a day at the Peoria Sports Complex and did not want to search for a restaurant off the premises. We ate at the Cantina which served Mexican food. The restaurant is pretty small and sits on a level above the bar area. The staff and the food were great. We hardly ordered before the food came out. We enjoyed the fried ice cream with strawberries for dessert.In the end, we would not hestitate to stay here again. We have already told several people about it. We got a great rate through Hilton's website at $178/night.

<Author>historyteacher
<Content>Not Up To Hilton Standards Last year in Feb., we stayed at the Hilton in Cabo San Lucas and I must admit, when we arrived at the Tapatio, we were extremely disappointed. For the same price per night, you cannot even compare the hotels. First, we arrived early on a Thursday and were informed that our room would not be ready until 4 pm. We basically wasted the first day of our trip (and the best weather day) waiting in the lobby for our room to be ready, even though we were told it would be ready by noon. The front desk staff was rude and sarcastic, which made matters worse. I have never had that problem at a Hilton. While we were waiting, we ate at the outdoor cafe, Cascades, and the food was horrible--stay away from the fish tacos which were merely fried pieces of crunchy batter. The rooms need to be updated and they were pretty drab--old couches and furniture--nothing fancy. The bed, however, was comfortable. The housecleaning servce leaves a lot to be desired. Finally, there is nothing to do at the hotel and they are pretty stingy with any kind of shuttle service. We rented a car for the day just to get off the grounds. On the plus side, there are pools and spas all over which are nice, although most of the lounge chairs are uncomfortable and do not have cushions. They also pass out regular, scratchy, non absorbent towels and not plush beach towels at the pool. There is an exercise room which is average-a few machines. The Point In Thyme restaurant was nice and room service was good. We did not eat at the Mexican restaurant. The Spa was nice and the body wrap was a nice experience but the Spa was definitely average and the place and the rooms were small. The view from our room was really pretty, we stayed in building 8 on the second floor and we overlooked the Falls village. We actually did not mind the walk around the resort but a resort shuttle is available. I am not a spoiled princess by any means but for the price we payed, 279.00/night, I definitely expected more luxury. I stayed at a Hilton in New Orleans, post Katrina, for 99$ a night and had more comfort. We also recently stayed at a Hilton in San Francisco for $119 a night and had a lot more luxury and comfort. The reviews on this hotel are mixed and I can see why and I am generally easy to please. I would not stay at this Hilton again, I also have a friend that stayed and felt the same way. Good Luck!

<Author>GreybeardCanuck
<Content>Excellent Experience! We just returned from a five-day stay at Tapatio Cliffs. We booked the hotel largely on the basis of positive Trip Advisor reviews, and were not disappointed.The resort is set out, as noted in other reviews, over 65 acres and is a series of two to four story buildings. All of the rooms are suites (I believe) and have spacious balconies. The suite we had featured a large living room with full-sized couch, TV, mini-bar, arm chair and desk. There were double doors that lead to a divided bathroom, then a sliding door through to the bedroom. This worked very well in terms of providing an environment in which I could work and my wife could sleep undisturbed. The room was clean and well appointed, and featured a comfortable king-size bed and a second TV. The resort also has a large water park with several pools spread over the property.We booked the romance package for $219 a night - this included a full breakfast for each of us (valued up to $44 combined), bottle of champagne, a two for one coupon for dinner and free use of the workout room (normally $10). A very good value compared to other prices we noted for similar hotels.The resort is in the northern part of Phoenix (25 min. drive to airport) and is built on a rocky bluff, so some of the rooms are a bit of a hike, although staff will pick you up and shuttle you anywhere you wish to go in the resort.If you want to be close to the Scottsdale shops and restaurants this is probably not the best choice for you. We drove to old town Scottsdale in about 25-30 minutes using the city streets rather than freeways. We preferred the rather secluded atmosphere of the resort but this may not work for everyone.There are three main restaurants on site plus a cafe by the main pool- we ate several time at Pointe in Thyme (main restaurant) and the breakfast were fine; average I suppose. We read good reviews of the mexican restaurant (nice balcony to sit on) but did not dine there. The upscale restaurant Different Pointe of View has an unbelievable view over Phoenix - even if you don't eat there go up before sunset and see the view. Our meal was excellent but not cheap- lobster with scallops ($42) was very nice and the lobster bisque was as good as I have had. Note: there is also an outside deck one level lower for the lounge, so if you don't want to spring for dinner, this is a good second choice.The staff were very helpful at the front desk and concierge desk. We would definitely stay here again when we return to Phoenix.  
<Date>Feb 25, 2007

<Author>iloveolives
<Content>Highly recommended We happended to be there for New Year's and there was a lot of bustle and excitement with the Festiva Bowl game - staff handled it really well. We had booked at the Pointe in Thyme and didn't realise what a big deal the NY's eve dinner was ( or the price) but it was worth it. The views were sensational as was the 5 course dinner and service. The resort is set into a cliff side so the rooms are in rows dotted along the windy little roads which made it very interesting. The room was excellent, with a separate sitting area with a bathroom between it and the bedroom with 2 doors, so you could easily stay up late to watch TV without disturbing anyone sleeping. The beds were v. comfortable with lots of pillows to make reading in bed comfortable. As we were there on NY's eve and the night of the Bowl with dozens of Boise and O S supporters running around it was a real testament to the soundproofing - there was no noise at all! The bathroom was a bit tiny but had a huge separate basin, dressing table area. The Crabtree and Eveylyn bath products were a nice touch. Room service was excellent ( and fast). Guest laundry was just around the corner. The pool we used was clean and well set out.

<Author>TravelEscape
<Content>Tapatio Cliffs Wonderful! Everyone of the staff we encountered were very helpful and friendly. Easy check in and check out. I was looking for a true suite, not just a room divided by a half wall, which gives no privacy. This Hilton knew how to do it right. There were 3 rooms, divided by doors for privacy, which is great when traveling with children or snorers (we had both). We entered the living room, which had a couch bed. The next room had a vanity on one side and behind closed doors on the other side were the toilet and bathtub. We continued on to a large bedroom with a balcony. The beds were super comfortable. We asked Room Service for additional towels, lotions, etc., and it was no problem at all.The casual Mexican Restaurant on property was very good and the cheaper of the more upscale restaurants (I forget the name) had a beautiful fireplace and a good meal. The drinks, however, were not the best, on the night we went.The only downside to staying at the Tapatio Cliffs is that it is all by itself. Not close to shopping, museums, etc. So it is perfect for a quiet getaway but if you want to do more, it's best to rent a car. We used their towncar service one night (rates slightly higher than a cab) and although it was cozy -- Super expensive. The hotel does provide a shuttle for $9.00 to the closest (upscale) mall but it is on a schedule i.e.; leave hotel at 11:30 a.m., return at 3:15 p.m. They also provide shuttle service onsite to your rooms and their restaurants (which came in handy in 30 degree temperatures at night). Just be prepared to tip.All in all, it lived up to the Hilton name. We were extremely happy with our room. It was my first time in Phoenix in the winter and even though outside it was freezing, the central heat worked great and we were not cold inside.

<Author>ypsilan
<Content>Great customer service Pro's: 1) Noteworthy customer service Every staff member that we encountered was friendly and efficient. They must have tons of employees all over the property because even though the property is spread out, they always addressed my concerns very promptly. After expressing some concerns about the food to our waiter at the Different Pointe of View restaurant, the manager came to talk to us about it and gave us a discount off the bill.  2) Good rooms for the price ($159/night) My suite was roomy and I really appreciated the separate living room area. The rooms are not ultra-posh but definitely nice enough and impeccably clean. It met my standards and was appropriate for the price point, if not better than most.  3) Comfy bed!Con's: 1) The exterior is a little dated and worn. Not enough to bother me.  2) The setting didn't appeal to me. It was just set in some brown dirt hills. I thought the cliffs would be more majestic. Maybe I don't appreciate the desert much, but it just looked like the hotel was put in one of the less-nice areas of where I come from (southern CA). 3) Food is not great. Some room service dishes were decent, others were not much better than the Olive Garden. Also ate at Different Pointe of View. I could not understand how my vegetarian dish could be worth $26. Tiny nouveau portions and bland, bland, bland. As mentioned above, the manager did address our concerns. The view and the restaurant and lounge itself were nice, though.Overall, I would not hesitate to stay here again for about the same price. I was very comfortable here for 4 nights. I will recommend it to my friends. I didn't try out the pools, spa or exercise area. Although it was fine for me, I can see where parking might be a problem.

<Author>Paris0618
<Content>Wonderful weekend at Pointe Hilton The Pointe Hilton was a great place for a girls weekend getaway! We arrived at night, and in the morning we walked the property to get our bearings. The resort is gorgeous! Our suite was on the 'mountainside' area, very quiet and up on the hill. We walked down the hill, found the pools, workout area, and restaurants. Our suite was very nice, well decorated and very clean. The staff at this resort couldn't have been more pleasant, from check in to room service to the concierge. We did use the free shuttle service to get around the resort a few times, and this was easy and quick.We dined at Pointe in Thyme upon our arrival, for a late snack and drinks, and I would recommend it (except for the occasional smoker!). For breakfast, we had bagels and cappucino from the lobby store, and brought these out on the patio overlooking the adult pool. And our last night, we dined at Different Pointe of View at the top of the cliffs. We had early reservations, 5:45, so that we could see the sunset, and watch the city of Phoenix change colors. The restaruant is a bit pricey, but the food and service were excellent, and the view.... perfect!We enjoyed the pools, and went to the Falls pool (a little noisy) and the lower pool (very quiet). We recommend the strawberry margaritas while lounging by the water here.Other recommendations while in Phoenix: hike Camelback mountain early in the morning, visit the Phoenix Museum of History in Heritage Square and have lunch in the Arizona Center close by, visit Frank Lloyd Wright's Taliesin West, and if you're a pizza lover as we are, definitely go to Pizza Bianco, also in Heritage Square! It was wonderful and worth the 1 hour wait!

<Author>ruthbern
<Content>Good for families We just returned from a 4 night summer stay at the Pointe. At the summer rate of $99 per night this hotel is a great deal and good for families. The 2-room suites are very much in the Embassy Suites style and quality. Nothing special, but nice to have the extra space for either a family or business traveler (I wouldn't call it resort quality). We requested and got a pull out sofa in the living room for the kids. It also had a small, but nice, balcony. Perfect for watching the amazing monsoon thunderstorms. The swimming pools are great for kids. The restaurant by the pool is nothing special, but perfect for a relaxing lunch or dinner while the kids swim. They call the Falls a water park. It's really just 2 big swimming pools and one water slide. Not a water park, but still, a great place to swim for my kids that aren't around pools much and it's easy to keep an eye on them. The resort has a nice little work-out room, but unfortunately they charge an extra $10 per day to use it. The best thing about the resort is that it sits on the Phoenix desert preserve. You can hike for miles, right from the hotel, in beautiful natural desert. Yes, you can also play golf and tennis, but the desert is a real treat. The down side of this hotel is that the restaurants are very expensive. I guess that it to be expected, but if you don't want to spend the money, there many inexpensive places within a short drive (great inexpensive Mexican food just a few blocks south on 7th street).

<Author>caligirl07
<Content>nice hotel We just returned from 4 days at the Pointe Tapatio Cliffs. It is a beautiful resort, although a bit dated. We were advised by staff members that it will recieve a face-lift next year. It is VERY hilly as mentioned by others. If your not into walking hills to get around, it may not be the best choice, although they do offer shuttle (golf cart) service from restaurants, etc. The restaurants were just average. Very helpful staff members throughout. If you enjoy hiking, there are great trails right off the resort. We went with our kids (12  14) who were bored after a couple of days. It seemed to be more familes with young children there. We did visit the sister property, Squaw Peak, again shuttle service provided. Although not as pretty, our kids had much more fun there. Older kids and much more to do around the pool area. If you're staying with children, ask for a room in The Falls or family pool area - it's much closer than the other suites. We would probably not stay here again. Not because we experienced anything bad, but because there are so many options in this area, we would want to try something else.

<Author>summergirl711
<Content>Great pools!! Relaxing vacation! My husband and I stayed at this resort June 3rd through the 9th. We were basically just going off the reviews from this website and had never been there before. We really enjoyed our vacation there. I love the southwest heat and love to be by the pool. This was the perfect place for that. If you are expecting the Four Seasons or the Fairmont, this is not it. This resort is nice, pretty, clean, comfortable, affordable, and above average.We had a suite that was very comfortable. The bed and pillows were incredible! We had a seperate bar and office area in the suite and a nice patio. The pools were wonderful! We mostly went to the pool next to the gym almost every day. They had a small lunch spot there that offered pizza, ice cream, snacks, and best of all, frozen magaritas! That pool was never croweded. We also tried the waterpark pool. It, of course, was a lot more crowded and lots of kids, as expected. They too, had a great lunch spot. We played golf at the course associated with the resort. Get ready for lots of bunnies roaming along the fairways and greens! We experienced a lot a nature that day. It was nice and the views were incredible! (Just tee off early because of the heat) Our only complaint was that the closest ice machine was not working for most of our stay. They had room service bring us ice which was ok. This resort is very convenient to grocery stores, Target, Walgreens, Starbucks, etc. Yes, it is a real hike to get back to your room, if you're staying up high. Overall, we would definately go back. It was perfect for us, and it didn't cost us an arm and a leg.

<Content>Great Place for Families Stayed here on June 22, 2006 for one night. We had a room in the 4000 wing on the top floor. The view from the balcony was of a tent building put up in the parking lot but that was no biggy. The room is nice and large. A queen sofa sleeper in the livingroom, and we had two queens in the bedroom. The bathroom are was a good size. Toilet, tub and shower on one side of the hallway and dressing sink and mirror on the other. The shampoos and lotions were really nice also. You can close off the livingroom area from the bathroom area and then there is a pocket door that you can also close off the bedroom area from the bathroom area. So its very nice and privite for all sleepers. The water park of the resort was nice. The servers there were prompt and very nice. The towels are plentiful also. The water slide was a blast (and Im an older woman) but I had a blast with the kids on that. The pool was relaxing and fun also. Lots of room to roam around and not be crowded. The desk help was great but the bell hops werent that super. They didnt seem to want to do much for you if you werent having them park your car. Beleive me, park your own car though, there's plenty of parking. We ate at the Mexican restraraunt and had great service and it wasnt priced to high either. The other pools on the property were nice too and hardly crowded at all. We stayed here before staying at the Westin in Scottsdale for two nights and we all agreed that the HIlton was more fun for all of us. We will go back for sure.

<Author>jolinegk
<Content>Good place to swim First of all, the place is huge and on the side of a mountain and we didn't see very much of it. When we arrived, it took three clerks to check us in, they kept looking at the screen with worried faces. Apparently, they had overbooked the suite near the Falls (the hotel waterpark) we requested. Instead, they upgraded us to the Ambassador suite, which is right across the road from the Falls. It provides shade, a fan, fridge, bowl of fruit and water bottles and much better lounge chairs. Plus the service seems to be better here. Be aware that we paid $81 for ours because it was Memorial Day weekend, so it may not be worth the price for some. I liked feeling like we had our own place instead of crowded in with all the rest.The kids loved the pools and slides. I found the water chilly, a little too flecked with leaves and the pool floor rough.

<Content>Disappointment We were expecting a nice resort but all we really got was an overglorified hotel. We were put in a Mountainside Suite which was supposed to be one of the better rooms. There was a big bag of garbage sitting right outside our door as we tried to get in the room. As soon as we entered the room, we noticed a very musty smell and also discovered that the toilet ran. We had a view of the Sunset Pool. Beware, it's very small and there's a very limited amount of chairs around it.We tried to make the best of our vacation by walking around the resort to see if we could find some good in the place. Big bags of garbage were laying around in many of the hallways around the resort and with the heat, you can imagine the smell. First, we stopped at the Point in Thyme restaurant because we were hungry. The place was almost empty yet it took over a 1/2 hour just to get our drink order......and then another 1/2 hr to get the sandwiches we ordered. We then thought we'd check out the spa. Wow, the smell of acrylic nail chemicals hits you as soon as you walk in the door. We moved on to check out the pools in the Falls Water Village. Now granted, we were there during Memorial Day weekend so we had a feeling it would be pretty busy but what a zoo! There were so many people jammed into the pool that they were on top of each other. Even the Grotto Pool which was supposedly the Adult Pool (i.e. quieter pool) had screaming kids everywhere. Nighttime wasn't much better. Again, lots of people screaming in the pools or running down the halls late at night. We ordered room service and the food was lousy. I guess if you have kids, then you're used to a lot of noise and this would be the hotel for you since it 's geared towards them. If you're looking for a relaxing, nice resort---this isn't the place. We've stayed at very nice Hilton hotels in Mexico and Hawaii. This place was a dump compared to those places. We left after one night.

<Content>Obviously water issues on site.... The con's:Two separate rooms booked, two toilets overflowed/stopped up. We used another at the pool for 2 iced teas (free refills), 2 kid drinks, a pretzel, nachos, wings, kid chicken tenders and a beer + pina colada. Another for lunch at Point in Tyme (3 beef sandwiches, kids meals + soft drinks) and one for breakfast (not sure what they ordered that time). The food was all good (not great, but definitely edible and convenient).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort I have stayed at this resort several times over the last several years. Unfortunately this year the resort has taken a severe nose dive and I will no longer stay there or recommend it to my friends. When I go to a resort I expect a certain standard. I'm paying to be pampered and feel as if I am in a luxurious location. I had always felt that way here until this past trip in late May. The resort no longer feels that way and it simply looks very tired and well past prime. The clientele has started the change from upscale to one notch above trailer trash (at least that is what I think of couples who become intimate in the pool in front of 50 others, mothers who allow children to run loose and then scream at them across the pool at the top of their lungs...not once but constantly, and families who check in with more food items than luggage (there are no cooking facilities in the rooms either). This is just a tired, rundown property. The outside needs to be spiffed up, the furniture and carpet in the rooms looks worn and shabby, the water in the main pool did not appear clean, and the staff while friendly appeared pre-occuped. The rooms were kept clean and the food was average. The bad now outweighs the good and we are switching locations.

<Author>operagirl1970
<Content>Great value and location We stayed here for a long weekend May 12-15 because of a great deal we got on Priceline. Not knowing what to expect, we were pleasantly surprised by the location, rooms and staff service. We were in one of the mountainside suites, which was located in a quieter area away from the main building. Even though we had a bit of a walk to the main pool area, it was right next to a very enjoyable smaller pool that was much quieter than the main pool/waterfall area if you're looking for a way to get away from the noise of kids (they were packed on Mother's Day weekend). We thoroughly enjoyed getting up in the morning and following the walking trails that connected to the resort near the tennis courts -- very convenient without having to cross busy traffic. Get up early though if you want to avoid extreme heat! The room itself was very clean with modern furnishings and the most comfortable bed I have ever slept on in a hotel! Having a balcony was a treat for when we came back from walking or the pool to just hang out and enjoy the mountains in the distance. While there were some spots that looked a tad dated around the resort, it was beautifully landscaped and the staff all had smiles on their faces and cheer in their voices. Because it is built into the side of a mountain, there are lots of hills and a twisting parking lot, but don't let that deter you if you don't mind the exercise.While we didn't eat at the resort, we found some GREAT restaurants within a 15 minute drive (we rented a car). Carolina's is a small short-order Mexican restaurant that is only about a 5-minute drive away on Cactus Road (go north from the resort on 7th St and turn right on Thunderbird/Cactus. I think it's at the intersection of Cactus and Cave Creek.) They had the BEST flour tortillas -- wafer thin, delicate, and huge. I can see why people drive from a distance just to take some home. It's very affordable too. My husband and I ate there on multiple occasions, and each time our bill ranged from $9-$14 for the two of us. For finer dining, we also went to a little place called Coup des Tartes on N.16th St. It's a small house converted into an elegantly romantic French restaurant. They don't have a liquor license, so you're encouraged to bring your own wine, which many people were doing. A grocery store is just north of the resort, so we were able to bring some too. The food was stellar, using the freshest ingredients. I highly recommend their signature lamb dish and the roquefort salad. Be sure to save room for dessert; you'll want their homemade tarts like the lemon tart with meringue four inches tall. Our final dinner was spent at a place called Richardson's that the concierge recommended. It's specialty is Southwest food, and while the concierge warned us that the place would look like a seedy bar when we first pulled up, the food is amazing. He was right! Both places were pricier, but the food was outstanding at both.If you get a chance, take a side trip to Scottsdale to the Frank Lloyd Wright estate for one of their nighttime tours. It was less than 30 minutes from the resort and the estate and architecture school lit up at night (plus the 2 hour tour) are well worth it. All in all, our stay at the hotel exceeded our expectations. We would definitely recommend staying there!  
<Date>May 17, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beware--buy from Priceline and be treated like a second class citizen My husband got this room for me and my friend as an early Mother's Day gift. On at least three occasions we told them that the whole purpose of the trip was to have 5 hours of peace and quiet with no children to watch a special DVD miniseries my friend received as a gift. We asked two different front desk employees about DVD players in the room and said to both that it was not a problem if they did not have a DVD player as we would just bring our own. We even had this conversation with the very nice person who checked us in. Needless to say, at 5 pm when we tried to connect our DVD player, we found out that there was absolutely no way to connect our DVD player to use the line in on the hotel TV because of the hotel's contract with their media provider. If someone had mentioned this to us, we could have planned accordingly and brought our own TV (though this seems rediculous to have to do). The manager on duty (Dan Nichols (spelling?)) was rude to my friend and dismissive. After another call and about an hour and a half, they offered us a solution...they could bring us a DVD player that would work on their TV's, BUT--it would cost an additional $85! You have got to be kidding me? $85 to use their DVD player for 5 hours? Why even offer that? Well...what could we expect for what we were paying for the room since we got it from Priceline? Too bad so sad for us. Why sell your rooms on Priceline if you are going to snub the guests who buy them? If you don't want cheepos like us there...don't sell the rooms on discount sites. Aside from the poor customer service, the beds were comfortable and room was clean if somewhat old. Shower head was excellent---finally a shower where I could rinse my hair in less than 10 minutes! The Works restaurant and arcade was an unattended counter and circa 1983 Centepede and Ms. Pac Man game. We were glad we did not bring the kids for that. Property is very hilly which is nice for views, but terrible for parking. Very narrow one way streets require detours around the whole property to get to your room or long walks with luggage. Water falls were nice. Pools were older and not nearly as specatacular as they appeared in photos. I think the usual price for our room was about $250. It was definitely NOT worth that. If you can get a deal, don't expect customer service, and don't mind having the fact that you purchased on Priceline pointed out to you several times as if you might be contagious...then this is the place for you.

<Content>Definetely not for Business Travel I made the mistake of staying here for business travel last month. I had originally intended to stay at the other Hilton Hotel, the Squaw Peak, but they were overbooked, so I stayed here because its only a few miles away.Here's the problem. You have to drive everywhere! Once you register at the front desk, you drive up to your building and look for parking. Then you drive to the restaurants (which were fair, although I didn't try the restaurant at the top which is supposedly very good), to the health center, etc. Its not that its that far to walk, but not when you're in a hurry. The room was adequate. There is nothing about this hotel that is designed for business traveler. As far as a resort, I would say this place is alright. Seems like a decent place for kids. Certainly not luxury by any measure. If you're looking for luxury, try the Four Seasons, Ritz or Phoenician.

<Author>Wisconsinfamily
<Content>very nice family resort Our family of 4, kids 11 and 9 stayed at Tapatio for 8 nights. We really enjoyed our stay. Room was clean, nicely furnished-newer decor, perfectly located in main building close walking to waterpark pool (The Falls). Food at resort was pricey, but your at a resort not McDonalds. Food was very good, better than average. The Pointe of View restaurant had an amazing view and great food, very pricey but a great way to end our vacation. Staff was attentive and helpful, never had one problem or complaint. Our room was always cleaned promptly and never saw the housekeeper. I guess the previous negative reviews gave me the feeling of uncertainty when we first arrived, but like I said we had a great experience. The resort is in a great location, easy to get to main highway to go to Scottsdale and area sights. The mountain trail hike adjacent to resort was wonderful. We did hit the local grocery for snacks, fruit and bottled water. Kids eat constantly, and mine are sometimes pickey. For the price we paid for this resort I feel it was a great.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Water, Water Everywhere... ! ME: 33yrs old, Gay male with partner, light travel for business. My partner and I were visiting family in the Phoenix area and stayed at the Tapatio. Though our stay was only one night, we instantly felt like we were on a wonderful 10-day vacation--- it was so relaxing!The LOCATION of the hotel is awesome - North Phoenix in a hilly residential area, just a few minutes from the freeway, downtown Phx and a quick drive to shops and restaurants. Though the property is expansive, it wasn't as ominous as it appeared on the map given to us upon check-in. It is, however, quite hilly as mentioned by previous reviewers. As for our ROOM, we stayed in the Cliffside Building in room 6225 (1 King bed suite) high above the rest of the resort. Our building felt very secluded and private, built along the rugged mountainside with a great view from our private patio. It was short walk from our room to the lobby andThe Falls/Water Village (about 6-mins.). We had lots of fluffy down pillows and a down comforter that made the bed a dream to stay in (BTW, a hypo-allergenic foam pillow was inside the closet just in case we weren't fond of feathers). The room was tastefully decorated, clean and in full working order. Parking was fine, except when we came home late night and had to park up by the Differrent POV restaurant, a short but STEEP walk up/down-- I guess I really am out of shape! Though we didn't use the shuttle, there were plenty riding around the property. Probably the best part of our stay was the pool... or POOLS. There were pools everywhere! My partner and I were in the mood to be total loungers and to just relax, eat, drink and swim. After we checked in, we immediate went to The Falls/Water Village for a swim. The Water Village is made up of two big pool areas - one with a waterslide, grottos and a mini-beach (no sand, just an ascending floor) and another more shaded pool with less hustle-n-bustle - both surrounded by beautiful landscaping, private cabanas and numerous waterfalls. The Cascade pool bar/cafe had great 'foofy' tropical drinks, light food and great service. We decided to pull a Burt Lancaster and swim in each pool --- I think there were 8! The great thing about this resort is that there are plenty of pools to choose from, depending on your mood: The big, busy pools for families, hanging with friends or to people watch; separate kid-free adult pools as well as semi- private pools with jacuzzis ('our' pool was the Sunset pool just below our room). All were easy to reach and stocked with plenty of fresh towels. Unlike another reviewer, I liked the waterslide and wasn't bothered by its design--- c'mon, man... it's a perk not a required amenity. Though we didn't take advantage of it, we were told by the Cafe that we also had access to the pools at the neighboring Hilton/Squaw Peak if we wanted. Overall, our stay was awesome: Friendly, knowledgeable staff; beautifully maintained grounds; great location; excellent room; great value for the price. We will definitely stay here again on our next visit to Phoenix.  
<Date>Apr 24, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved this resort! What a wonderful place to stay with children! The rooms have a perfect set-up (especially for those that still nap), the staff is extremely accomodating and timely on all requests, the food is well-priced (particularly the kids' menus - all items $5), and the family golf lesson was just wonderful! Our room was quite a ways from The Falls (main pool area, which is kids' heaven for swimming), but the shuttles were quick and it is not a long walk (very nice walk, if you like hills). The pool near our room was perfect for a quick swim or to take a hot tub. We even ordered a pizza there and ate by the pool and it was just delightful. The workout room is free, clean, nice, and also has a nice sauna. We hiked North Mountain across the street (even pushed the stroller - trail was paved), went to a Wild Animal Zoo, hiked right behind the resort, did a family golf lesson, played tennis, ping pong, had faces painted, watermelon eating contests, and enjoyed the pool! This resort caters to families of all ages and everyone was so happy there! The only not-terrific event was eating dinner at Point in Thyme. Overpriced, took too long with kids, and the food wasn't very good. Highly recommend this resort to families with children!!

<Author>swirlinabc
<Content>A very pleasant stay We took our 8 and 6 year old daughters on Spring Break for this trip. There are 8 different pools. One is adults only; the others are for both kids and adults. We managed to experience all of them during the trip! My six year old wanted to try them all (except the adult pool for 16 and over).The main pool at the Falls Village was great for families with kids. Lots of poolside lounge chairs, lots of umbrellas. Nearby the water slide. The grotto pool at the Falls Village is nice, but less shade. Other than the family pool at the main building, the remaining pools are small, but suitable for a quick dip and not laps. The best thing about Falls Village is the ability of ordering food and drink by simply putting up the flag on your chair.We were originally checked into room 4052. This room faced the laundry area, making the patio worthless. Avoid the eastern side of the main building to avoid the laundry area and noisy fans. (Fortunately) the hot water was faulty in the shower, so we got moved to 6224 on the cliffside suites. The hotel was also very kind to credit us the price of our breakfast to compensate for the inconvenience. This was a much nicer room (though slightly smaller)with a gorgeous view and steps from the sunset pool. I agree with the previous poster that navigating your way through the resort is a challenge. The maps are sometimes confusing and don't necessarily take into account the hills. However, enjoying a challenge, I eventually figured out the most efficient way to get from area to area. This is not for everyone however. For those who don't like to navigate hills and a maze of paths, the resort does offer several pick up points that will send a driver with a phone call.Food was basically average at best. First morning we had breakfast at the Point in Tyme restaurant. Service was lousy, and food only so-so. The Cascades restaurant at the Falls Village was okay, and convenient to order by simply putting up your flag for service. We had breakfast buffet at La Cantina which was of lesser quality than Point in Tyme. We never tried any dinners on-site because they really aren't geared towards kids. Very surprising for a resort that has such a family draw. We did not try the Different Pointe of View at the top of the hill as this was highly priced and definitely not kid friendly.We did have breakfast twice at a local restaurant called Pinky's just down the hill from the resort on the corner of Thunderbird and 7th. This was very good and half the price of the resort. Other mornings we purchased bagels, yogurt and fruit from the Safeway next to Pinkys and at it on our patio with the great view. Paradise Valley Mall is nearby that has a wide selection of known chain restaurants, including Marie Callendars, Olive Garden, Outback Steakhouse, and Chilis. Overall food review...unless you are transportation challenged, dine outside the resort if you have kids.In summary, we had a great time at Tapatio Cliffs. Service was very nice, pools are very enjoyable. Food really could be improved, particularly if you travel with kids.  
<Date>Apr 18, 2006

<Author>travlinstan
<Content>spring break in AZ First about me:- Normally only stay in hotels on business- Not a frequent traveler- looking for fun in the sun with my teenage daughters on this tripThe Hotel- Has a central building and several outlying 'villas' nestled into the hills- Room was nice and spacious and had the ability for privacy in the bedroom, bath/toilet, vanity/sink, and livingroom.- Hiking trails on nature preserve and interpretive center within walking distanceComments- The nicest place I have stayed regarding amenities, facilities and setting. The pools and lanscaping are fabulous! Room layout was perfect for our family situation.- For a place this large and complicated, the staff should try a little harder to explain how to use it. I mentioned this was my first visit to both the front desk and bell captain, all I was offered was directions to my room. I had to probe for the rest and wss often give conflicting info.- Loved the Falls Village pool area. It was really geared for (and primarily used by) families with kids under 12. But we were escaping the rainy CA Bay Area so this was just the ticket. On our day of checkout rented a cabana for $50 so were able to stay the entire day in comfort with food, phone, TV and pool.- Biggest complaint was noisy neighbors on last night (college boys on spring break deciding to party in the room). I complained to front desk and they said they would take care of it, but they were at it less than an hour later. - Ate at Falls Village Cafe and The Cantina. Service was good at F.V. but lousy at Cantina. Food just average at both.- Lamp in LR was broken so lamp shade hung to one side. Toilet backed up (did I mention I have two girls?) but was fixed very quickly by uniformed service man. Other minor things that I would have tried to get fixed if we stayed longer.Overall- We liked it. My girls were very impressed and my elder daughter said she'd like to come back as an adult. For me the access to pool, golf, hiking, and the room layout were just what I wanted. As with any place, some staff were more helpful, friendly, than others. This is a big place with many facilites spread out over a large area. I think they keep this place running quite well and have it properly staffed (approx. 80% occupied during our stay). For $60 more a night than staying at a Embassy Suites, I think this was well worth the money.

<Content>great resort We stayed at this resort for 3 nights. The landscaping was very beautiful. There were many pools and it was optimal to be able to choose whether to be at a noisy pool with kids running around or relax at a quiet pool with only adults. <Author>Danny5566
<Content>Met our expectations We stayed at Tapatio Cliffs four nights in late March 2006 and enjoyed it. Picked it largely for the pools and were not disappointed. The steel drum and marimba duo were a pleasant surprise. Lots of fountains--all working. And the landscaping was immaculate. Also, the small sunset pool and hot tub closer to our room were very nice and open late at night.This is a VERY hilly property, which helps make it scenic, but I'd be hesitant to recommend it to anyone not sure-footed, at least in the upper buildings. While we were generally able to park pretty close to our room, there were severe inclines to navigate going to the car.As expected, there was a $10 daily charge for high-speed internet, which seems stingy for a hotel in this price range. We were also put off by the charge to use the exercise room. Hilton should realize this kind of nickle-and-diming can take the luster off an otherwise very positive experience.If we return to Phoenix, we'll strongly consider this resort again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Relaxing retreat My wife and I just returned from a wonderful week at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort. The resort is set in a beautiful location nestled in the hills of northern Phoenix. Our suite had a spacious living room connected through a two-section bathroom to a large bedroom, and had a balcony with views of the surrounding mountains. The room and whole resort were impeccably clean and the furnishings were nice but not ornate. The staff was noticeably friendly, more so than at other resorts where we have stayed.The workout center is moderate-sized and has excellent equipment. I enjoyed running in the Phoenix Mountain Preserve, which connects directly to the resort, and allows you to experience a real desert environment. We also took advantage of using the sister property at Squaw Peak, which had a larger waterpark, mini-golf, and a larger workout center. We got the sense that Squaw Peak was more family-oriented, whereas Tapatio was more geared for couples and corporate retreats, although both properties were equally nice. On our last night, we had a fabulous dinner at the Different Pointe of View restaurant, which was pricey but did have excellent food, and the views of the surrounding hills and the city are unparalleled.The downsides we can think of were that it was sometimes a little noisy around the resort with all the cleaning (street sweeping, leaf-blowing, etc.). Also, the resort is built on a large hillside, which affords excellent views, but could make it difficult to get around for less fit visitors. My wife and I enjoyed this layout, as it built a little exercise into our day. The resort does offer shuttle service, which we used once and found to be very efficient and easy. Finding parking was never a problem. We enjoyed exploring nearby Scottsdale, but did find it to be a bit far from the resort (about a 30 min. drive with no easy highway connections). We brought our laptop but had to pay $10/day to get high-speed internet access in our room. Also, a $9/day per room resort fee is added to the charges if you wish to use the fitness center and some of the other amenties such as mini-golf.These were minor complaints, and overall, we would whole-heartedly recommend Tapatio Cliffs, and would definitely stay here again when returning to the Phoenix area.  
<Date>Mar 11, 2006

<Author>BuckeyeBob
<Content>Great Start to the New Year Stayed here while visiting for the 2006 Fiesta Bowl. The property is an easy drive north of town ( about 12 miles from Sky Harbour, I think). A nicely different hotel layout built into the cliff sides presents an out of the ordinary lodging experience with numerous detached buildings. A series of walkways and foot bridges connects many of the buildings. The parking, as noted by many others, can be tricky, but is one the quirks that makes the property different and memorable. Enjoyed dining at all the venues at the property with great food and decent service. The mountaintop restaurant was TOP NOTCH in every detail for exquisitely fine dining with a spectacular view. On site shuttle was helpful for getting around the property, especially if your lady is dressed for dinner and walking shoes aren't part of the package. The variety of pool areas offer something for everyone. Only sorry I did not get to try the golf course which got nice reviews from those that I encountered who did play it.

<Author>JTro
<Content>Great Holiday! My husband and I stayed at this hotel from Oct 23 - 26th. From the moment we arrived the customer service was excellent! At check in, the woman at the front desk suggested a couple of areas for us as to where our room could be located, so we choose to stay in the 2100 block - not in the main building but close enought to walk to the Falls pool area. This proved to be a perfect location for us. We easily got a parking spot in front of our building block each night. Our room was great, air conditioned, comfortable and decorated nicely. About 30 mins after we got into our room, a hotel worker stopped by to make sure everything was okay and whether we had any questions. I was very impressed with that. We mixed our holiday with pool time at the Falls -- very nice there, some kids were playing in the pool, but hey, that's what kids do in a pool! Noted, it wasn't overly croweded there at this time of year, but that was just bonus for us. We also golfed at the Lookout course --which was beautiful and in great shape for October. We ate breakfast every morning at the Point in Thyme restaurant and thought the food was great and priced reasonably. We also had dinner at the Different Pointe of View our first night there. We drove up to the restaurant and the views were amazing! The food is pricey but worth every penny. Definitely not a kids restaurant. I know that there have been some complaints about this place and I'm a very picky person too so I went there with fairly neutral feelings about the hotel. But, honestly, I think people complain just to hear themselves complain. If you are a person with limited mobility and don't like to walk around, then this obviously isn't the place for you, however, I'd hope that in this day and age, you'd have access to the internet to see that this hotel wouldn't be suitable in advance of going there. As well, the parking could be a problem I suppose, but again, if you don't mind walking from your spot, it's not a big deal. This hotel definitely has the feel of an old spanish village, hacienda style with all of the narrow, winding roads. I found this to be charming. The location of the hotel seemed reasonable to me as well. We got around fine, and found to give 20mins or so to get anywhere. We had planned to eat our meals at the hotel or near where we were sightseeing, so didn't find this to be a problem. All in all, I would stay here again. We really enjoyed it. By the way, my husband and I are 30, and are fairly well travelled.  
<Date>Oct 27, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Gave it a second chance, would never go back We stayed at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs over the July 4th weekend for the first time with two other families. The rooms here are quite large and perfect for families with children. Parking is a nightmare though. We rented a private poolside cabana for two days, which was great to have with small children. The pool area looks very nice and is clean, but this weekend it was completely overrun with people who were not guests of the hotel. We knoe this for a fact, as we learned this from the people directly. As a result, the poolside service they promised was dismal at best. On more than one occasion, we placed food and beverage orders and had to chase down the wait staff to find out where our orders were. Lunch on the first day took over an hour, only to have the wrong food arrive. It went on in this same vein for the remainder of the weekend, also at the other restaurants on the property. We made the mistake of ordering room service for breakfast one morning and by the time the food arrived, it was cold and we were missing items (like butter and syrup for pancakes). The staff kept offering apologies simply by informing us how busy they were.I ended up writing a letter to the hotel, and I was sent a very nice response with a promise of a free room, if we would give them another try. We thought why not.We visited over Labor Day weekend and it seemed much less crowded. They were checking names at the gate to the main pool/waterfall/slide area so non paying guests wouldn't be able to use the facilities. This was definitely a step in the right direction. We also rented a poolside cabana for the day. The day started out fantastic, but as soon as our waitress went off duty, we never saw another poolside attendant for the remainder of the day. That evening there was a rain storm and as a result, the ceiling in the bedroom not only leaked extensively, large chunks of plaster started to fall on the bed! This was at 10:00 PM-not pleasant, especially as our children woke up at this point. It was impossible to sleep in the bedroom, due to the noise of the water dripping....something like water torture. We called the front office and they offered to send down a cot-which would do what, we wondered as there were 4 of us. We had to move to a new room, which for anyone traveling with small children, wasn't easy to do at that time of night, having to pack up all our belongings, etc. The next day, they offered a $50 credit towards the room (we stayed an additional night beyond the previously comped room) and when I let them know that wasn't good enough given what we had been through the previous night, they agreed to give us the room for the night at no charge, plus the $50 credit toward food. I was pleased. Until we got our credit card bill and we discovered we were in fact charged for the room.Long story short, they are claiming they never promised the free room as they would never have done such a thing-they only give small credit toward the total room bill itself. Given the fact this was our third such poor service experience at a Hilton property, we have since canceled our frequent traveler account with Hilton and would never use their properties again.

<Author>MelisM_TX
<Content>Exception Service My stay at the Pointe Hilton resort was related to a conference at the same location. Although the location is a bit out-of-the-way to downtown Phoenix and Scottsdale (at least a 20 minute drive from resort), it was very convenient to stay at the same property as the conference. I traveled with several team members and we decided to take advantage of us being in the same place to have meetings in one of the rooms so we booked the presidential suite. The room was arranged with a screen, projector and flip chart per our request as soon as we checked in. And with any request (i.e. a longer phone cord to stretch the phone to the table), someone came to the room in less than 10 minutes to help. This is no small feat considering the property is spread over several levels and waundering roads. The service was exceptional as we were able to order food for breakfast and lunch for 8 people and receive everything in less than 30 minutes. And it was all delicious!A previous review mentioned the Falls area and I highly recommend that as well. It was so quiet in that section except for the sound of the waterfall outside our doors. I enjoyed the suite layout of the room so that I could use my laptop in the living section of the room and keep the bedroom area for sleeping. Although Phoenix was still a bit warm, I was able to keep my room quite cool and comfortable and the bed was very comfortable and inviting.Although we did not get a chance to enjoy the facilities for golf or swimming, those areas looked nice as well. The exterior of some buildings are a bit worn but the interior is clean and very nice for the price.

<Content>Nice hotel I stayed August 27-29 on business. Nice hotel, very spread out, which I did not expect. I had asked for a room near the main building so I wouldn't have to walk very far to and fro during the evening. There is a nice gift shop in the main building that sells snacks, drinks and some breakfast items like bagels and croissants.I would stay there again. Interesting location in the cliffs and good service. There is highspeed internet capability in each guest room, which was convenient.

<Content>Nothing to write home about... I stayed at this hotel with my colleagues for 5 weeks in July. As part of the well respected Hilton family we did expect to get an upgrade (we were all silver/gold members), but the response was that it would be too unprofitable for them to give us an upgdare - there goes putting valuable customers first!The rooms were OK - they do need refurbishment...particularly bathrooms. And the aircon was a problem for each one of us (there were 5 of us)...so when you check in to your room - turn the aircon off and wait for 20 seconds: in 3 of our rooms there was a terrible bang every time the aircon was switched off...and the fault could not be repairedThe pools were another story - they were FILTHY! Im not going to go into details....but I guess seeing flocks of long hairs all around you and the water being slightly yellow in colour says it all!Apparently July in Phoenix was low season (we come from Europe, hence July is THE SEASON!) so breakfast buffet was only served over the week end and during the week it was a la carte....and it was terrible!! each table had 3 waiters: 1 to sit you, 1 to take drink orders, 1 to take food orders - THEY COULD NOT MULTITASK! when you asked the drinks boy to order food you could see hysteria coming over his face! it took us 1 hour to order fruit/cereal and the prices were well over the roof!I must say I expected a lot more from a Hilton....they have another resort nearby called Sqauw Peak - and that's much nicer!

<Author>audreyliz
<Content>Resort for families and groups of kids My husband and I stayed at this facility for 4 nights in July 2005. I chose this location because I was able to get 2 free nights using my Hilton Honors points. I paid $89/night for the other 2 nights, so I averaged $45/night. Considering what I paid for this hotel, it was quite a bargain. However, I would not stay here again if I had to pay more than $100/night.This hotel caters to and attracts LOTS of kids. There were times that it felt like a day care center. And as is typical of parents on vacation with their kids, most of the kids were allowed to run rampant like wild animals. They even invaded the Adult Pool which is clearly labeled as such and the parents watched as their darlings dove, yes dove, in to 4ft deep water. The kids also took over the restaurant during the morning breakfast buffet and created a madhouse. I even saw a kid pick up a donut, take a bite out of it, and put it back in the basket. Fortunately a server saw this and promptly whisked away the whole basket. Another kid was running his fingers through the diced green peppers at the omelette table and his mother said, I quote, Don't touch that, you'll get it on your clothes!So you can see this is not the place for adults without children or anyone who values hygiene and safety. In general, the rooms were spacious and averagly furnished. They do seem a bit old and not well-maintained. The property is very spread out and you have to walk quite far to get places or you can call for hotel transportation or drive your own car. The Pointe in Thyme restaurant is WAY OVERPRICED, and I suggest finding your breakfast at offsite locations. There is a Village Inn about 2 miles north on 7th, a Denny's about 1 mile west on Cactus, and an IHOP about 5 miles west on Cactus. Don't go there for lunch or dinner either. The Cantina was pretty tasty, but also overpriced. 2 adults can share a burrito and be full. The Different Pointe of View restaurant was spectacular and well worth it. If you are going to be enjoying libations poolside, I recommend going to the Safeway down the street, buying your beverages there, along with some insulated mugs, and storing them in your mini-bar fridge. Instant savings!The spa was very professional and the services were luxurious. However, the description on the website of the body treatments, such as the masks and wraps, does not mention that they include the body brushing that is part of the Body Glow treatment. I signed up for both, received both in succession, then discovered that I paid $65 for something that would have been included in my Seaweed wrap anyway. That was sort of depressing, but I figured that at least I got an additional 20 minutes of massage.So, to sum up, only go here if you have kids and want to let them run wild. Different Pointe of View is worth visiting even if you are not staying here. And don't buy a Body Glow treatment if you are getting a wrap!

<Content>Beautiful resort, wonderful pools, fantastic bellman We just returned from a 4 night stay. Our very kind bellman, Dick, then drove us up the cliffs and carried our bags again in the heat to a suite with a beautiful view. Hilton certainly has a fantastic employee in Dick. He knew we were ready to leave the Tapatio Cliffs and find something else, but he was so kind pointing out all the good features of the hotel. We were so happy with our suite with the view, all our bad thoughts about the resort quickly disappeared. Dick then called us when he got back down to the front desk to assure us that we could have the suite for our 4 nights and not have to move to less expensive room the next day.  When we return to Phoenix, we will definitely want to stay at the Cliffs, and will probably pay the extra money for the view. It was so wonderful to sit on the patio and drink coffee early in the morning and enjoy that view.Thanks to Dick for sticking with us and seeing we were happy with our room. Hilton is very fortunate to have an employee who represented them very well (unlike the front staff).

<Author>maroulni
<Content>Beautiful Grounds, Okay Service We just returned from 6 nights at the Tapatio Cliffs Resort, which were pleasurable, and very reasonably priced, considering the summer rates available at the resort. This resort is very large, however, and the service suffers.We had booked a rate of $89 plus tax through the Hilton website. Though we had requested a king bed, a standard king bedded room was not available at check-in. Rather, we were put in a handicapped accessible room, which, given its functional necessities, was not as luxurious as a standard room (e.g. awkward shower instead of bath, etc.) We requested a room change for the next day, and were accomodated. Because we were going to be spending the majority of our time off-resort, we requested a room in the main building, which was close to the elevators and complimentary valet, which made for easy exits and arrivals.Though the main building did not have the views of some of the other suites, it's convenience was an asset to us. I would recommend the main building for those who might have trouble getting around a sprawling resort, or who prefer the convenience of being close to their cars.The pool areas are diverse, with an adult pool behind the main building, and additional family geared pools scattered around the resort. The Falls complex has a nice atmosphere, with great bar service, and a fun enclosed waterslide.We did have problems with the service. The ice machines were either missing or inoperable around our room, so we requested that ice be brought to our room. Almost an hour later, it arrived. On another occasion, an important fax arrived for us and while the front desk called to tell us they would happily deliver it to our room immediately, it took amost an hour to arrive. Other than these types of issues, our stay was pleasant. We would recommend the Tapatio Cliffs resort for families and easygoing people who enjoy swimming and the added room provided by an all suite resort.

<Content>Wonderful time at the Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort My husband and I just returned from a stay at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort last week. After reading some of the reviews on Trip Advisor, I was a bit concerned. <Author>cathykins
<Content>Nice, older place with a lot of charm My husband and I stayed here in April and the weather was perfect. We stayed in Room 4133 with a Valley view. The room itself has a very small separate bedroom and then a little living room. There are two t.v.s. I found the room to be a little dark actually, and I have seen that comment on here before. However, the bed was wonderfully comfortable and we liked our balcony and the sitting area.There are a number of different pool areas and one day we used the very quiet one by our room and the next day we went to the more family oriented larger area which offered drink service. Both were nice in their own way. We ate dinner the first night at a Different Pointe of View and the view is spectacular and the food was excellent. Really recommend it.The only negative about the place was all the walking one would have to do. Parking is at a premium so you may not be able to park very close to your room. For us, that is no problem but I kept wondering about elderly people. I could see my folks not being happy about it.Overall the service was great (we had two room-service breakfasts delivered hot and on time) and the dinner we ate there was excellent. It is a charming place that meanders up a hillside and we would stay there again.

<Author>UCLaw98
<Content>Great Hotel - Need Quieter Golf Carts We just returned from our second of two stays at the Tapatio Cliffs, the first was in November '04 Overall, I would recommend this resort. Both stays our room was great - very spacious (suite) for what we paid ($99/night the first stay; Corp. Rate of $129 the second stay), very comfortable beds (down comforter/pillows), extremely clean, great views from the balcony or windows, good sound insulation between rooms.I like the fact that the resort is spread out and is on a hilly area because it lends to more character than a block-building hotel, the buildings are spread out and there are a number of pool areas which allow for more or less relaxation depending on what type of activities you desire.The only annoying thing is the gas-powered golf carts that zip around the resort delivering luggage/people/room service. They are incredibly noisy, kind of like a lawn mower sound, so you don't want to leave your sliding door open while trying to sleep! They are also not that careful about going around the many corners, so you have to be very careful when walking around the resort to avoid being run over! It would be a good idea for them to replace the carts with electric-powered (quieter) ones.The first time we went, we went hiking and there are nice hiking trails (moderately difficult) that are accessible near the tennis courts.The second time we visited, we had dinner at a Different Pointe of View and the view was AMAZING, it was very romantic and the food was great - interesting combinations of ingredients and great service. It is expensive though, so if on a budget, try the bar area for a drink, the views are worth it!They have a shuttle which will pick you up at your room and take you around the resort, which was great because my boyfriend hurt his ankle (and I was in heels), so they chauffered us to dinner and back.The staff here was helpful anytime we had questions or problems.I had trouble finding a soda machine near the pool that was working and when I called to complain, they said that if it was convenient, I could just take sodas from the mini-bar in our room and they wouldn't charge us. It was a great solution and I appreciated that they didn't argue or give me a hard time, but just solved the problem.We stayed there primarily because it's near relatives, but I would recommend it to anyone who finds a reasonable rate and is staying in the Phoenix area. There's also a Starbucks and Walgreens right down the road, which was great!

<Author>vicki1812
<Content>very disappointing - not 5 star Following a 10 day trip driving around Arizona we decided to end with a stay at this advertised luxury 5 star resort, but were very disappointed. Previoulsy we have stayed at the Fairmont scottsdale princess  the Biltmore, both in Scottsdale. Firstly the resort is huge - 585 rooms and very impersonal. People at the check in desk were very impersonal (I am a silver VIP member of Hilton's loyalty club) and mistakes were made on our booking, with no hint of apology. We had booked a romance package which included a premium suite with view, champagne and b/fast. We had to ask repeatedly for the wine and as they do not have 24 hour room service then we missed our pre paid b/fast as we had an early flight, as this resort is a good 25/30 minute drive from Phoenix Airport - don't believe the blurb that is it closer. When we asked the resort staff if they could organise something for us they said no! No assistance was offered with bags and the bell desk was unhelpful and gave wrong info.The room (No.4130) was Ok - nothing special, although it was quite spacious. We did have a view - but we also had a view of the air con units and they were very noisy at night. The bathroom was small  basic and the bath was just a standard issue with very low  small hotel bath - no good if you are over 4 feet. The suite was supposedly recently re modelled but the carpet was stained and furniture scratched, and hard to beleive but all of the ornaments/accesserioes were actually glued or nailed to the surfaces - and as we had booked a 5 star hotel and paid $280 for the package we were insuted that the hotel has pre decided that guests could not be trusted!This resort is called the ciffs for a reason - it is built into the side of a cliff and a lot of the suites are up several flights of stairs and along balconies, there are elevators but they are old and not located next to the suites. Parking is a nightmare - there are main carparks which are quite a way from the rooms but there are not enough car spaces for the suites within a close proximity. If you had a large car or had a lot of unloading to do or you have mobility problems then you may struggle. It took 10 minutes of very careful manovering to try and park our car in a very small space- very fustrating. Whist the resort grounds were well kept, the surrounding area was not great and we ended up traveling back to scottsdale to find somewhere where we wanted to eat. There are no faciities outside of the resort within walking distance and the area to the south is not one you would want to be in late at nightIn all very dissapointing, overpriced and we will not be returning. If we had another night in Phoenix we would stay at the Fairmont or the Biltmore both if which advertise great deals via their websites or Hotels. Scottsdale is a much better location for the airport and facilities, we are frequent international travellers and would not recommend this hotel.

<Author>bakery
<Content>Great stay at the Tapatio We just got back from three nights at this resort, and we really enjoyed our stay. We, too, found it quiet (even though our trip coincided with Arizona's March Break and there were probably more families than usual). Our suite was spacious, and not dated like some of the other reviewers have mentioned. Several earlier reviews mentioned a bee problem at the resort. I didn't find it to be a problem at all, although it may be seasonal. The pool with the water slide was great early in the day, but we found it excessively busy into the afternoon so we switched to the family pool in the main building. It was much quieter and made a nice change. We had breakfast there every day as we were on the BounceBack plan, and the buffet had a good variety of delicious food. The location of the resort is one of its biggest assets but also one of its biggest detriments. The upside is that it is beautifully situated, seemingly far from the busy city. The downside is that it is far from most of the good restaurants. (There's an Oregano's located about 15 minutes away that's very good.) Having said that, we had a great stay and would stay at this resort again if we went back to Phoenix.

<Author>PPop54
<Content>some good, some bad Stayed here for three days while participating in a business meeting. Didn't know what to expect after reading previous reviews. The good news was that the bed was extremely comfortable (nice linens, mattress similar in feel to comfy beds at W Hotels) and the room was probably one of the quietest hotel rooms I've stayed in (maybe we lucked out with quiet neighbors). When checking in, we did request that our room be in a quiet section of the property and we upgraded to a room with a view -- we were in the cliffside area above the Sunset Pool. Room was spacious, OK decor, but it's obvious that the property was built in the 1970s since bathtub, toilet, etc are all of a rather dated vintage. Our suite had open beam cathedral ceilings, which was nice, so I recommend requesting an upper unit. The downside: The resort seems very tired and dated, elevators run very slowly, everything seems a little bit patched together and in need of paint or a good makeover or remodel (I did notice those painted floor tiles in the lobby that someone mentioned, though I didn't think they looked that bad). Service in the restaurant by the pro shop was slow and food was substandard. Fish tacos at Mexican place were OK. Since hotel is built on a hillside, there's lots of walking involved if you are in an upper unit, but we didn't mind that at all -- a five-minute walk seemed better than being housed in one of the dreary units near the lobby that overlooked the parking lot. Another point (or pointe) to consider: Location of the hotel is not the best for accessing tourist venues (spring training, Scottsdale, etc. ). Overall, the property is dated, but our unit (at least) offered quiet, a comfy bed and a view (albeit of suburban sprawl and hills way beyond). I probably would not stay here again, but the stay could have been a whole lot worse -- at least we were able to sleep.
