<Author>dardo
<Content>It had everything plus a couple of unexpected bonuses. Just got back from 4 enjoyable nights at The Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort.  Incidentally it is pronounced tap as in ...'Golly, he is a good tap dancer. and patio as in St. Patrick. I find that pronouncing correctly the name of whereever I choose to lay my body down for sleep makes my lodging stay all the more delightful.Yes, I run the danger of sounding like a lodging snob but that's me and I can't help it. What's there not to like about the the place? Beats me. I had a suite with a living room with a couch and 2 chairs, a desk with internet hook up, a wet bar, entertainment center with a TV. The vestibule with the bath on one side and the sink on the other led to a very spacious bedroom with twin queen beds, another TV, plus a balcony that provided a splendid view to the north of the valley and mountains. Terrycloth robe too.The staff? ...a more congenial, helpful group you will not find. The only minor glitch is I had a little trouble finding my room initially but that was mainly because I am part of the great fraternity who do not like to ask for directions even though they gave me a map and directions. I've read the complaints about the parking. You're not going to find your typical parking lot here with herringbone spaces on a flat surface. In fact hilly parking outranks flat parking at this resort by at least 2 to 1. . They don't call it Tapatio Cliffs for nothing folks. For people who are not fond of walking a little or flat out hate it..especially uphill..then I can understand because you may have to park a little ways. But didn't I read somewhere where the Surgeon General highly recommends excersize like walking? The farthest I parked from my room was less than 75 yards. I've stayed at other hotels where it seemed that long just getting from my room to the elevator.For me the walking was a plus ...not just for the exercise but walking in a beautiful setting of Spanish architecture in natural southwest surroundings.. I particularly liked the heavy breathing hike to the top of the Pointe where you get a fabulous view of the city. Then there are the swimming pools...they are all over the place. I had one just a few steps from my door. I had come to Phoenix to take in Mariner spring training in suburban Peoria so when I got back after baseball and sightseeing it was a little too cool to take a dip so I can't give you my take on that but the pools looked inviting and they have waterfalls that cascade from one pool to another. There is even a water slide...so needless to say for kids this is a very cool place. There are also tennis courts and a golf course. I liked it that you could walk right off the resort property smack dab onto a desert hiking trail. I checked it out at dawn one morning and met up with some sociable rabbits. Another unexpected bonus..because Arizona had more than its share of rain this winter there was an abundance of wildflowers on the trail. The Pointe is like a Spanish village stuck velcro like on a hillside with fountains, tastefully landscaped, manicured lawns and gardens with all kinds of cacti, trees, and lovely flower beds. The Pointe has restaurants and bars. You have a Walgrens, MacDonalds, gas stations, and two supermarkets less than a mile down the hill on 7th. Unfortunately there is but one sit down restaurant in that neighborhood...Pinky's Cafe. I had breakfast there one morning (I was but one of two patrons in the restaurant ...a red flag I chose to ignore) and my scrambled eggs seemed to take forever to prepare no doubt coming from incompetant chickens so I would suggest you avoid the place. On the other hand Eddie and Mike's Pizza next to A.J''s Foods (in the strip mall to your left just before the traffic light at the bottom of the hill) is not only the most immaculate pizza parlor I have seen in a month or so but the pizza is very good and is alledgedly the world's best. I don't know about that but it is tasty and besides, the poeple who serve you are nice.I thought this was an excellent value especially for families and I wouldn't hesitate to recommend The Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs Resort. The staff will see my face there again.

<Author>Oregon Shelly
<Content>Not 5 star but still nice We just spent 5 nights at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs this past weekend while my husband attended a conference. Overall, we were happy with our stay. Here is a more detailed report of our experience:Good things:1. Our room was very spacious -- it was actually a 2 room suite with a bedroom and a separate living area and a wet bar. I've heard that all of the rooms at this hotel are set up like this. It was nice to have the extra space. My husband used the living area at night to watch TV so he wouldn't disturb me if I turned in early.2. Atmosphere -- although its an older property, this hotel is very beautiful. Driving up to our room, my husband and I felt like we were in a quaint Mexican village. The grounds looked especially nice this time of year since all of the flowers were in bloom. 3. Pool Area -- The Falls pool area was wonderful! Definitely my favorite part of the hotel! It was very clean and spacious with lots of places to lay out. The scenery was beautiful with the waterfalls surrounding the whole area. The pool snack bar -- Cascades Cafe was also very nice. I enjoyed many yummy poolside drinks and lunches there over the course of our stay. 4. Different Pointe of View -- Although we dropped over $200 here for dinner, it was definitely worth it!!! The view from this restaurant was unlike nothing I've ever seen -- absolutely breathtaking! We requested a table outside and got to enjoy the fabulous sunset. The food was excellent. I ordered the Chef's Menu Sampler -- a five course meal designed especially for me by the chef. It was outstanding!!Not so good things:1. Service -- I've stayed at other hotels in the Phoenix area where the staff was extremely friendly. Not the case at this hotel. I wouldn't say that they were rude, just not overly friendly. 2. Getting Around the Hotel -- the hotel is very spread out. Our room was located in the Mountainside Suites area and was halfway up the mountain. Luckily, the temperature was in the mid 70's. If if was in the 90's-100's, then it would have been a lot more difficult walking the steep road to our room. Also, the streets are very narrrow and there are not always sidewalks. I felt like I was constantly having to stop to let cars pass if I was walking. Overall, the good things outweigh the bad things. I would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great place We stayed here 3 nights at the end of February 2005, with a family of 4 (two kids aged 6 and 9). The one bedroom suite in building 5 of the Hidden Valley was classy, fairly large, mostly quiet and spotless. It was a bit tricky to find our room, even with their map. We got a package deal thru Costco Travel for around $550 for 3 nights. The beds were extremely comfortable. Be sure to ask for a room near The Falls if you have kids, as this place covers a lot of real estate and has hills and stairs.The restaurant near the pool had excellent food (from the kid stuff, burgers, exotic drinks to the spa-like salads) and the service was above average, especially Summer. The prices were quite reasonable. The restaurant near the golf course had very tasty food, but the service was a bit slow on both mornings and the one night we ate there. They seemed to be short staffed in the mornings. The breakfast buffet was outrageous at $18 for adults, but a steal at $5 for kids. The quality of food on the buffet was very good. We ate at the Mexican restaurant one night and it was reasonably priced, good service, but the food was only okay, not great. It was more of a sports bar atmosphere.The pools were very clean, uncrowded, plentiful and beautiful. We loved hearing the waterfalls. We took one look at the water slide and did not try it. It appeared too narrow for adults, and our girls were not interested in a dark fully enclosed black pipe. There were 2 boys around age 11, who were really enjoying it, however. We liked that we were able to borrow tennis rackets and balls and introduce our kids to tennis. They let us take the kids for a ride in the golf carts, also for free. Both my dad and my husband went for a 4 mile hike around a butte right from the door of the hotel. They said the views were very nice.Down the street a bit is a Starbucks, Target, Chili's, Boston Market, El Pollo Loco, and Sonic Burger.We also did a day trip to the Squaw Peak Point Hilton where there are reciprocal privileges. We had a car so we drove, but they have free shuttles between the hotels available. The Lazy River was as warm as bath water and only 3 ft deep (safe for our 6 year old). The current kept us going for about 15 minutes around the loop. We were not charged for the inner-tube. It was also not very busy at this Hilton. We played some miniature golf, and again no charge. Their water slide was fun for my 9 year old, but she said the water was cold (it was only around 65 degrees air temperature that day). They did not have much pool side service, and the food was not as healthy as the Tapatio. There were nets up for water volley ball. Their wild west theme was pretty cute.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent choice My husband and I just returned from a stay at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs. We chose the Pointe for its location and price and we were not disappointed at all. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Mixed Reviews? Here's why! This is a huge older property with a variety of accomadation types. At best it's a 2-3 star resort. There are alot of amenitites which will give you the impression that this is a great 4 star resort... it's not. It's carved out of the side of a rocky hill/mountain. There is no natural beauty anywhere to be found. The hillside suites are small, offer no view except of the parking stalls and other buildings. The views you do get are of the burb's rooftops, lots of city lights at night. Hiking trails lead to dirt paths... I have seen the desert, this isn't it. The highway runs right past it... it is NOT REMOTE in the sense of being off the beaten path, it's just inconvenientley out of the way. There are residential subdivisions and strip malls at the bottom of the hill. You might as well be half way up the space needle in Seattle. What ever desert terrain is left is devoid of life. I'm sure at one point, this was a wonderful spot surrounded by natural beauty but unfortunatley urban sprawl has taken over.The resort has not aged well either. The rooms are terribly outdated in decor, layout and size. Even the updated rooms have a bandaid feel with their mismatched furniture... this was done on the cheap. Everywhere I looked, I saw cheap fixes... the fountains patched with cement, the lobby terra cotta floor painted over to look new!... layers of paint everywhere...nothing flowed. Now if all this didn't catch your eye AND you got a cheap web rate (perhaps something you would pay at a 2-3 star hotel), you probably gave this place a positive review. However if you paid more than say $99.00/night then you felt ripped off like I did. I could have paid the same price and stayed at the Wig Wam (also an older resort but gorgeous) but was seduced by the phony marketing on the Pointe Hiltons' web site... thinking I was to expect 4 star quality... It looks good on the net but reality bites!The golf course is well manicured but it too has fallen victim to urban sprawl...traffic noise and backyard walls everywhere... too bad...it has some nice holes in the hills. We checked out early after 3 days of sunning and golf (that we did enjoy) and headed east to Fountain Hills. Ended up in the gorgeous Inn at Eagle Mountain...paid less too!! There are just too many better places to stay in Scottsdale and area that provide the 4-5 star experience.I've been on budget vacations and extravagant vacations... I didn't complain about either because I got what I expected. The Pointe Hilton is a fraud and that ticks me off. Stop pretending to be something you're not. You should be described as a larger perhaps upscale Ramada.Go on the cheap or don't go ... I think you'll be disappointed.  
<Date>Jan 12, 2005

<Author>skistopalms
<Content>Both pluses and minuses at Tapatio Cliffs... Sorry, but I cannot agree with the excellent ratings some have given this hillside property. On the plus side, the hillside European village layout of the property is charming, the pretty entrance and lobby have an upscale feel, the staff is friendly, caring and helpful (5-star quality!), and the suite-style rooms are spacious and clean -- except for patio furniture which was too dirty to use. But, the first room we were given smelled so overwhelmingly musty that we asked to be moved. Our 2nd room was better, but still had a bit of that musty smell, which the staff said comes from the A/C when a room is unoccupied for awhile. Our other disappointment was dinner at their La Cantina Mexican restaurant, where the cheese had an odd (cheap) imitation-cheese taste and texture. If you are traveling with children, then the water park and reasonably priced 2-room suites (we paid $104 on an August weekend) may override any other factors. But, if you're picky, as we are, Tapatio Cliffs Resort may not meet your expectations in all areas.  
<Date>Aug 27, 2004

<Author>grram1
<Content>Top notch family resort! This is a great place to vacation! The standard room is an embassy-suite style standard suite (separate bedroom/living room areas, nicely decorated and very comfortable). The staff if very friendly. The grounds are beautiful and there's tons of stuff to do! This is the most kid-friendly resort we've ever been to... there are free activities throughout the day for the kids and on Saturday nights they have a free pool side dive-in movie, there are about 8 pools, a water slide, and water falls and fountains located throughout. The kids get a free welcome gift. The only drawbacks are the cost of food (although this is typical of these types of properties), and parking is a bit of a hassle... but you can valet for the cost of a tip if you chose. They could use a few more strategically placed elevator too (depending on your room location you can be in for a bit of a walk if you need to use the elevators). Overall this was a great experience, and given the great deal we got through Hotwire at $75/night it was pretty amazing!

<Author>milhouse
<Content>Nothing Exciting Stayed here for one night before moving over to The Phoenician. While not bad, it certainly lacks many of the finer qualities of the area's better establishments (Four Seasons, Phoenician, Fairmont Scottsdale Princess). Located in a so so area of North Phoenix. The room itself had a popcorn ceiling and poorly textured walls. It struck me that if 6 Motel ever decided they wanted to go resort style this would be the place that they would open up. The comforter and bedding, as well as the entire interior, were all standard Hilton - nothing to connote the southwest (the comforter was a loudy itchy green floral print). The wash basin was also located in the bedroom (not in the bathroom) which struck me as odd and does not help matters when one person is an earlier riser than another. View = My wife and I were given a view which overlooked a parking lot and other peoples balconies. It's a good 20 minute drive to the center of Scottsdale (if you're looking to dine at one of the many fine dining spots in the Scottsdale area). While not bad for families looking to save a little, it is not the luxurious resort for which it bills itself. And it is far, very far, from being even one of the top 5-6 resorts in the area.

We bought bottled water and a cheap cooler, better than purchasing from the hotel, and you will drink lots. Just can't say enough good things, we all really enjoyed our 5 night stay!

<Content>Wonderful Stay! My husband and I just returned yesterday (6-7-04)from Tapatio Cliffs resort and had a wonderful time. The Falls Village water park was GREAT! It seemed like there were pools/Jacuzzis everywhere! The resort and rooms were very clean. Request a room by the falls if you plan on doing lots of swimming, otherwise you may have to walk a bit. Also, we went to Walgreens and purchased a small cooler and bottled water for a fraction of the price you would pay on the resort. You definitely need to drink LOTS of water with the high temp. Everyone at the resort was extremely helpful and friendly. The food there was great...a bit pricey but very good. There were some wasps outside of our room so we called to have them removed. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice stay but Squaw Peak has the edge... Stayed at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs May 6-11, 2004 for the first time. The suite was spacious and immaculate. Loved relaxing by the pool at The Falls as did my kids (ages 5 and 8). The slide is a blast. The food and drinks we ordered poolside were fine. There are an unusually high number of bees by the pool, so beware. The hotel is not in the nicest part of Phoenix. Driving from the Skytop airport to the hotel was depressing. Thankfully the hotel is very nice for a few days of relaxation. Visited the sister property, the Squaw Peak, and would have stayed there had we known. In short, everything was better (location, appearance, pool, the mini golf on premises, the tubing down a lazy river, the kids). If you're looking for a more relaxing time go to Tapatio, but if you're travelling w/kids, do the Squaw Peak.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Must read if you are considering this Resort After reading the other reviews, I felt I must submit. We have stayed at this resort 3X in the past 10 years. Our most recent to celebrate our 10th Anniv, incorporating a family vacation. The grounds are fabulous. Our room was cliffside with a view of the Presidential Pool on one side  panoramic view toward the west from our bedroom. I do feel the rooms are overpriced - the resort is beginning to show it's age - but I would still go back and always look for a good deal. Older people or anyone who is not physically fit should demand a Main Building room - the resort grounds will be a challenge otherwise. Getting around in your auto and parking are obnoxious - but unique and should be approached without expectations! I love a Diff Pte of View - however, not a family restaurant! My 17 yr old son could not find anything on the menu that appealed to him and the expert service made him uncomfortable. Very, very pricey, but my meal was fab.In a nutshell, this resort has something for everyone - romantic or family oriented. The Resort Golf Course is one of the best that we golfed, so do not disregard as an option.I agree with most of the reviews that if you can eat somewhere else - do it. It is very expensive at this resort (BLT poolside is $12 with automatic 18% tip)

<Author>ltp_tango
<Content>Better Places to Stay in Phoenix I stayed here in the summer of 2003 because a friend had a free voucher. Visitors to Phoenix and Scottsdale, please note: there are MANY, much better resorts to stay at than this one. This is an old property, with some maintenance problems. The water features are nice, but just average for Phoenix. This resort is kind of far from most tourist attractions, etc. For the money (about $100 a night from Memorial Day to Labor Day), try the JW Marriott Desert Ridge (which is a beautiful new resort in north Phoenix). All of the Phoenix and Scottsdale resorts have water features and most have golf courses, too, so shop around. It is a buyer's market with resorts in Phoenix during the summer.

<Author>LydsNJ
<Content>Great vacation at Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs We just got back from a 5 night stay at Tapatio Cliffs. We were able to check in at 10:00 am which gave us a full day at the hotel, rather than checking in at 4:00pm. I had requested a cliffside room and was a little disappointed when we were assigned a room at the Falls. After seeing our room location I was very happy. Our room overlooked the family pool and we had easy access to the restaurants, lobby and the Falls Pool. Being Hilton Honors members we were entitled to 2 bottles of water, use of the workout room at no extra charge (which we actually didn't use because it was a hike from our room), 2 vouchers for breakfast worth $11. 95 each day, and a 1:00 checkout (instead of noon). I agree that the rooms could use some updating such as the carpet and comforters, but they were clean and well maintained. The staff was very friendly and helpful. The grounds are beautiful, we hiked the nearby mountains (there is one beginner trail and two moderate-experienced trails). It was noisy at night because children were still at the family pool at 10:30 pm playing Marco Polo but that was the only real negative. Would definately return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Love the resort, rooms mediocre at best My family just returned from a week at The Pointe. The pools and the views we all loved especially my six year old. He had a blast. I enjoyed walking around the huge resort. We took SO MANY PICTURES. The Pointe is clean and the pools are abundant and beautiful. The location is great, close to Scottsdale (we went there a few nights for dinner). I was a little disappointed with our room however. I'm really ease to please I usually never complain but we had a running toilet that I had to call about several times. I also didn't love our view. We overlooked a parking lot. The room itself had a bizzare layout and I would rate the actual room medicore. However, the resort, the views, the pools, the lobby, etc etc made the weakness of the room go away. The pools are great for families. In short here is what you should stay away from @ The Pointe and here is what you should enjoy. Don't go to there Mexican restaurant. It is a poor man's sequel to Taco Bell and it is pricey. You should order lunch at The Falls (poolside), It is pricey but it is good and the service it great. You should drive up to a Different Point of View (Restaurant at the top of the Cliff (great views) take a view pictures up there. Everyone goes to The Falls (we did most of the week BUT the secret here is to go to the Family Pool. It is less crowded and it is beautiful. Try to get a room in the Cliffside or Mountainside area.. Don't get a room near the falls unless you want to overlook a parking lot and have your toilet running throughout your stay. In summary it was a lot of fun and I would go back. I would follow my own advice though. If you have kids who love fun in the sun this is a great place to get some r  r. Outside of the resort make sure you hit a place called Rawhide. It is a hoot (old western town we did there cookout and enjoyed the steakhouse.

<Author>kadie28
<Content>A great ACCESSIBLE getaway We recently spent 4 nights at the Tapatio Pointe Hilton Resort. It's a great place for kids and adults alike. There were days we wanted to spend at the resort itself (it has 8 pools - 4 small/fairly private with hottubs and 4 large with hottubs, 2 at the water park, one large family by the lobby and one large adult only pool with bar access). The resort has hiking within walking distance, stables next door and an award winning golf course. The food was tremendous though pricey as you would expect from hotel restaurants. They have a morning brunch that's DELICIOUS! The views, the hiking, the restaurants (four that I remember), the service, and the pools make it a memorable trip. It's also conveniently located - close to the airport, and almost all of the baseball stadiums are within 25 minutes drive. Scottsdale is close enough to visit and have lunch/dinner there as well. The Zoo and Botanical Gardens are about 25 minutes away and the travel is beautiful by Camelback. I would recommend a stay here to anyone.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>5th time here!! This is our 5th visit to a Pointe in Phoenix - 3 to Squaw Peak and 2 to Tapatio Cliffs. Reading some of the other reviews might make me choose a different location. But some of the reasons we choose this again and again are the very reasons why others disliked it. To each his own, I guess. We love the fact that this resort is on a cliff side - you can go any city and stay in a hotel that has rooms side by side down a hallway with an elevator. This one has meandering walkways and driveways with various sized buildings scattered over the side of the mountain. We actually stayed quite close to the Falls pool but took 1-2 walks everyday just to explore the grounds - my kids loved it and we went a different direction everytime. The kids were never bored there - lots of activities or just playing in the water. We have recommended this place to over 10 families over the years and all have loved it. Also, be sure to visit the pool at Squaw Peak - more of a 'water park' and quite busy - but again, the kids will love it! True, the prices aren't cheap, but we always go over spring break - the prices aren't cheap anywhere Phoenix - but that is what you have to pay to get out of the snow! Mini-bars are what you would expect in any hotel - if you don't want to pay for them, don't use them! Pools are all for no additional charge. The only resort charge is for the fitness center and tennis courts. We used both of these everyday - well worth the $9 per room fee! Restuarants are typical hotel cost and quality. Again - what were you expecting? We ate breakfast there everyday because we were anxious to get to the pools and activities for the day. At night, we generally chose to go off-campus and experience someplace else. Phoenix is not so big a town that you can't drive to very nice places within a short time - and while you are driving it gives you the chance to see the rest of the city. If you want to be pampered - choose one of the $400 per night luxury hotels. If you want to have a great family vacation and experience a unique location in Phoenix with something for everyone to do, choose the Pointe at Tapatio Cliffs.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice, but too pricey We stayed over a long weekend the end of January. I agree with others who rate this resort as average. Our room was nice with views, but it was a long walk to get to the lobby, restaurants and golf. Because the resort is build on a hillside, we had to walk down numerous stairs and take and elevator in an adjacent building. Finally, we just drove to save time. The restaurants are very pricey with mediocre food. I was charged $6.50 for a margarita in a plastic cup and a simple lunch cost us $35 with tip. We recommend you eat out. One reviewer mentioned El Bravo at 8338 7th street and we tried it. Modest decor, but very good food (we eat a lot of Mexican). A local took us to another place nearby called Via Delosantos (9120 N. Central) that was also very good and lots of fun. Margaritas are $2 and better than at the Hilton. The dinner for three was cheaper than a tuna sandwich lunch at the Hilton. If you like Mexican, both are very good.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice, but average I stayed here recently in mid-October and got a very good deal on a business government rate. The room was very spacious, the resort itself quite pleasant. However, if I had had to pay standard commercial rates, I would have to rate this property simply average for an advertised luxury resort. The newer resort hotels in nearby Scottsdale have far more to offer than the Pointe Hilton, particularly to adults traveling without children. The front desk here seemed a bit understaffed; I had to wait nearly 20 minutes to hand in my room key and get an updated bill receipt. The restaurant is pleasant, but nothing special, with eager to please staff actually becoming a bit intrusive to several business meetings. In spite of having a room with large wet bar and counter with bar stools, there was no microwave, small refrigerator or any other kitchen type amenities to make use of the expansive space for potential entertaining or snack preparation. This is a very good spot for families with children, especially given the pools and water recreation facilities. For business travelers or adults without children, there are nicer places for the same price or less.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Getaway Selected this resort as a freebie using my Hilton Honors points....wished I would have selected a different resort. Nice, quiet place, clean, friendly staff, good amenities, but no better than the average hotel chain. We encountered air conditioner problems and had to report the problem three times before it was fixed. Tips for the traveler.....ask for a room close to the lobby or the Falls Pool Area if you plan on using that pool and do not want to drive to the pool. The rooms that are higher in number, i.e. 5000, 6000 are very high up on the mountainside and a long way from the large pool area....rent a cabana by the Grotto pool - $35 well spent for the day if it is very hot and sunny....El Bravo Mexican Restaurant located on same street as resort (south of) is a diner-like restaurant but has the best Mexican food I've ever tasted....go to Wal-Mart about 10 minutes north of the resort and buy your own bottled water and snacks....wake by 6:00 in the morning and head out for a hike on the trail accessible by the tennis courts. Absolutely beautiful and not too hot in the morning. We saw coyote on two different mornings.

<Author>CNorm
<Content>A pleasant resort Just returned from a too short 3-night stay at the Pointe Hilton Tapatio Cliffs with my 3 sisters. It's a lovely and pleasant resort which, at first, seems daunting from the site map the front desk provides at check-in. However, that turned out not to be the case at all. It was actually quite easy to get around this spread out resort, which has many pools (there is a main one with waterfalls and a slide) and hot tubs. And depending on the time of year you go, you may find a pool all to yourself. The resort is set up like a small community, where you park your car (you will need a car to get around as the resort is not walking distance to anything...Scottsdale shopping is a 25-minute drive away, as are good restaurants) in front of your room. The rooms are comfortably furnished in a tasteful southwestern theme. We ate at 2 of the 4 restaurants on the property, i.e. the most affordable ones, where the prices were quite fair. We did not venture into the 2 most expensive ones. Since 2 of us are very into working out, it was well worth the $9/day (not per person, but per room) for use of the well-equipped fitness center. We did encounter a minor problem in our room (which we only realized when we went to take showers before heading out to dinner the 1st night) which resulted in a room change. But the staff was extremely accommodating (including extra blankets, pillows and towels) and made the change right away. I am not one to complain just b/c something went wrong at a hotel/resort. As long as the problem is quickly and properly rectified, the property did its job. Not every room can be perfect all the time. A quick note: Sedona was only a 90-minute drive from the Tapatio Cliffs. Go there...very well worth the trip. Simply beautiful.  
<Date>Oct 16, 2003

<Author>bigbucksfan
<Content>Great Place, Great Service My daughter and I stayed here for five nights in April. The hotel and grounds were beautiful and the service and staff were wonderful from check-in to check-out. My experience with their service and staff (very important to me as a single Mom): I was a little concerned because I had gotten a great rate on Priceline, however at check-in no mention or attitude whatsoever of Priceline, the rate, etc. The young lady that helped us asked if I had a HiltonHonors card and noted it on the reservation -I didn't get any points for the stay, but they did provide a couple of free bottles of water. She also explained and gave me the OPTION of paying for the $9 (I think) day resort charge for use of the fitness area, tennis courts, etc. As we were only planning on using the pools we did not have to pay. Best of all she gave us a great room in the building directly behind a main parking lot, very close to the Falls pool, main building, etc. Upon reaching our room and unpacking I called housekeeping to report a burnt out light bulb and to request a new air filter. The light bulb arrived within 15 minutes and the air filter was changed within about 2 hours! I thought that the daily housekeeping did a great job. Most days my daughter and I hung out at the pools and then went exploring (Scottsdale) in the evenings. Service at the main pools was always good, helpful and friendly. A few times they refilled our lemonades without charging. Additionally, the last day we were there we hung out at one of the smaller pools (the Sunset Pool is the best) and ordered room service for lunch, which was delivered quickly. Two other notable experiences -the last evening we were there I contacted the concierge desk to request to use their business office to check-in online for our return flights the next day. The office closes at 6:00 pm, but they told me that I could see the concierge anytime and he could let me in. He did so around 7:30 pm and made sure that I got connected and then left us -just told me to shut and lock the door behind me. (I'm not sure if there was supposed to be a cost...but I wasn't charged anything). And finally, upon return from dinner at a wonderful Italian restaurant (recommended by the same concierge) I decided to take my daughter up to the Different Pointe of View restaurant for dessert (I had read about their Bananas Foster). It was very late when we arrived and they were obviously winding down for the night... I was expecting to get a polite sorry, too late especially for a request for just dessert, with a child (low $). The maitre'd told us that certainly we could have dessert and we could sit anywhere we liked (there's a wall of windows that overlooks the city). He and the staff then set-up the entire routine to prepare the bananas foster (it's done table-side). My daughter loved it. The price wasn't cheap...but I wasn't expecting it to be. And considering the service we received it was worth every penny.The resort itself is beautiful and well-maintained. I would recommend walking around to the different pools to see the views. The hike on the hill was also fun and interesting. Small note-we drove over to their sister property (Squaw Peak) to check out the water park. For me it seemed a little too amusement park-ish (great for kids) and the actual rooms/buildings seemed to be sprawled out, not as intimate as Tapatio Cliffs.We will definitely try and go back soon.

<Author>valleykat
<Content>Great Summer Rates Family Friendly We stayed one night in late June, 2003, at the Tapatio Cliffs. Like a previous reviewer, our room which I booked from their on-line site, was less than $90, a super rate for this quality of a place. We arrived early and were able to check in no problem. Based on some reviews I had read, we requested a room near the Falls pool, as we expected to spend most of our time there. We were given a room next to the Family pool, a good location with a short walk to the Falls pool, but we were unfortunately stuck in a corner room with no view, front or rear. That was the only negative aspect of our stay, and since we only stayed one night, it was not a big deal. I would recommend a cliff's room unless walking is really a hardship. Many of them are still convenient to the Falls pool and the views are very nice. The room was very spacious and accomodated our family of five nicely; there was even comfortable seating for all of us to watch TV together in the living area; a rare thing in these suite rooms from my experience. I was most impressed with the beds. They were by far the most comfortable hotel beds I have slept in and the pillows were cozy down.The Falls pool was great, not too crowded on the Thursday we stayed. There were plenty of lounge chairs which was a problem we encountered at the Hilton in Sedona later on our trip. It was over 100 degrees outside, but as long as you took a dip every so often, it was comfortable as there was a nice breeze, and the temperature of the Falls pools was refreshingly cool due to the waterfalls. I think the hilly location of this resort, as opposed to the nearby Pointe Hilton Squaw Peak, gives the Tapatio Cliffs an advantage. The drinks at the pool were too costly for our budget, but they have ice water available throughout the pool area at no charge. For younger families, there were free activities for kids adjacent to the Falls pool every hour on the hour, like arts and crafts, hula hoop contests, a visit from a local zoo, etc. There were also ping pong tables, foose ball, and a basketball court for older kids. They had a special summer package which included a free gift for the kids, a free Icee, and a bargain room service dinner offer, among other things. We had pizza, chicken wings and a liter of soda delivered to our room for only $19.99. We walked the entire resort in the evening so my daughter could put her foot in each of their 8 pools. My husband and son took an early morning hike on their hiking trail. Even though they charge for late check-out, their check out time is not until 12 pm so we were still able to enjoy a couple of hours at the pool before we left on Friday. I highly recommend the Tapatio Cliffs for a family stay.  
<Date>Jul 5, 2003
